## ταβέρνη (id: 004903000000000)

ταβέρνη
=======

noun\-name, f. \| \-ης

7\.11 · Constructions · Buildings

inn a place for the lodging of travellers ταβέρνη occurs in the NT only as a part of a place name, Τριῶν Ταβερνῶν ‘Three Taverns’ ([ACT 28:15](https://ref.ly/John28:15)).

[ACT 28:15](https://ref.ly/John28:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 28:15

## ταλαντιαῖος (id: 004911000000000)

ταλαντιαῖος
===========

ταλαντιαῖος (G5006)

adjc. \| \-α, \-ον \| τάλαντον

86\.5 · Weight · Pound, Talent \[Specific Units of Weight]

weighing a talent pertaining to weighing a talent or 125 Roman pounds of twelve ounces each or approximately ninety pounds (English weight) or forty kilograms It may, however, be better to use in [REV 16:21](https://ref.ly/Jude16:21) an expression with a more general sense, for example, ‘great stones of hail weighing almost a hundred pounds’ or ‘... forty kilos.’

[REV 16:21](https://ref.ly/Jude16:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 16:21


## τάλαντον (id: 004912000000000)

τάλαντον
========

τάλαντον (G5007)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| ταλαντιαῖος

6\.82 · Artifacts · Money and Monetary Units

talent a Greek monetary unit (also a unit of weight) with a value which fluctuated, depending upon the particular monetary system which prevailed at a particular period of time (a silver talent was worth approximately six thousand denarii with gold talents worth at least thirty times that much) In [MAT 25:15](https://ref.ly/Matt25:15) what is important is the relative number of talents or sums of money. In a number of translations the respective amounts are stated in terms of local currency. For example, in English one may speak of five thousand dollars as equivalent to five talents, though in terms of buying power, five talents would be worth much more than five thousand dollars. What is important, however, in this story is not the precise sums of money but the relative amount which was given to the different servants.  
The ‘ten thousand talents’ referred to in [MAT 18:24](https://ref.ly/Matt18:24) would be equivalent to millions of denarii. The sum in this parable is perhaps greatly exaggerated, precisely in order to emphasize the vast differences between the two debts. It is also true, of course, that in ancient times persons with extensive mercantile businesses sometimes became slaves as a result of defeat in war, and they were purchased by business syndicates together with their business enterprises, which they would continue to manage.

[MAT 18:24](https://ref.ly/Matt18:24) · [MAT 25:15](https://ref.ly/Matt25:15) · [MAT 25:16](https://ref.ly/Matt25:16) · [MAT 25:20](https://ref.ly/Matt25:20) · [MAT 25:20](https://ref.ly/Matt25:20) · [MAT 25:20](https://ref.ly/Matt25:20) · [MAT 25:20](https://ref.ly/Matt25:20) · [MAT 25:22](https://ref.ly/Matt25:22) · [MAT 25:22](https://ref.ly/Matt25:22) · [MAT 25:22](https://ref.ly/Matt25:22) · [MAT 25:24](https://ref.ly/Matt25:24) · [MAT 25:25](https://ref.ly/Matt25:25) · [MAT 25:28](https://ref.ly/Matt25:28) · [MAT 25:28](https://ref.ly/Matt25:28)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 18:24; Matthew 25:15; Matthew 25:16; Matthew 25:20; Matthew 25:22; Matthew 25:24; Matthew 25:25; Matthew 25:28

[MRK 5:41](https://ref.ly/Matt5:41)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 5:41


## ταμεῖον (id: 004914000000000)

ταμεῖον
=======

ταμεῖον (G5009)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| ταμιεύω (be a manager or steward)

7\.28 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

inner room a room in the interior of a house, normally without windows opening to the outside In [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3) the emphasis is upon the strictly private location of the inner room. In such a context one may translate ‘a strictly private room’ or ‘a small room in the center of the house.’

[MAT 6:6](https://ref.ly/Matt6:6) · [MAT 24:26](https://ref.ly/Matt24:26) · [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3)

7\.32 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

storeroom, treasure room a room for the storage of valuables ταμεῖον\[b] and θησαυρός\[a] may often be rendered by descriptive phrases, for example, ‘a room where valuable things are kept’ or ‘a place where valuables are stored.’  
In [MAT 12:35](https://ref.ly/Matt12:35) θησαυρός\[a] is used figuratively (ὁ ἀγαθὸς ἄνθρωπος ἐκ τοῦ ἀγαθοῦ θησαυροῦ ἐκβάλλει ἀγαθά ‘a good man draws good things from his good storehouse,’ meaning ‘... storehouse of good things’) to describe the heart as a kind of storehouse or treasure.

[LUK 12:24](https://ref.ly/Mark12:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:6; Matthew 24:26; Luke 12:3; Luke 12:24


## τάξις (id: 004915000000000)

τάξις
=====

τάξις (G5010)

noun, f. \| \-εως \| τάσσω

61\.3 · Sequence

in order, in a sequence an ordered or arranged sequence

[LUK 1:8](https://ref.ly/Mark1:8)

62\.7 · Arrange, Organize · Organize \[of events and states]

right order, good order, in order, in an orderly manner a proper and correct order In [COL 2:5](https://ref.ly/Phil2:5) τάξις may refer to the orderly manner in which the church at Colossae conducted its affairs or carried on its worship.

[1CO 14:40](https://ref.ly/Rom14:40) · [COL 2:5](https://ref.ly/Phil2:5)

58\.21 · Nature, Class, Example · Class, Kind

kind, type kind or type of entity, implying a contrast\-comparison to other similar entities It is possible that τάξις in [HEB 5:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:6) refers to a kind of priest on the basis of being in a particular grouping or order of priests, but there seems to be no reference to any higher rank or position.

[HEB 5:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:6) · [HEB 5:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:10) · [HEB 6:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:20) · [HEB 7:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:11) · [HEB 7:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:11) · [HEB 7:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:17)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:8; 1 Corinthians 14:40; Colossians 2:5; Hebrews 5:6; Hebrews 5:10; Hebrews 6:20; Hebrews 7:11; Hebrews 7:17


## ταπεινός (id: 004916000000000)

ταπεινός
========

ταπεινός (G5011)

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| ταπεινόω

25\.295 · Attitudes and Emotions · Discouragement

dejected, downheearted, downcast (compare ταπεινός\[c] ‘of low status,’ [87\.61](#87.61)) pertaining to being discouraged and lacking in hope, with the possible implication of some association with low social status

[2CO 7:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:6)

88\.52 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Humility

humble pertaining to being unpretentious in one’s behavior In some languages the expression ‘humble in spirit’ or ‘humble in heart’ may be expressed as ‘speaking only soft words’ or ‘without shouting at others.’

[MAT 11:29](https://ref.ly/Matt11:29) · [JAS 4:6](https://ref.ly/Heb4:6) · [1PE 5:5](https://ref.ly/Jas5:5)

87\.61 · Status · Low Status or Rank \[including persons of low status]

lowly, humble pertaining to having low and humble status

[LUK 1:52](https://ref.ly/Mark1:52) · [ROM 12:16](https://ref.ly/Acts12:16) · [JAS 1:9](https://ref.ly/Heb1:9)

88\.64 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Gentleness, Mildness

gentle, meek and mild pertaining to being meek, with the implication of low status

[2CO 10:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:1)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 7:6; Matthew 11:29; James 4:6; 1 Peter 5:5; Luke 1:52; Romans 12:16; James 1:9; 2 Corinthians 10:1


## ταπεινοφροσύνη (id: 004917000000000)

ταπεινοφροσύνη
==============

ταπεινοφροσύνη (G5012)

noun, f. \| \-ης \| ταπεινόω \+ φρονέω

88\.53 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Humility

humble attitude, humility, without arrogance the quality of humility The rendering of ταπεινοφροσύνη in [COL 2:18](https://ref.ly/Phil2:18) as ‘false humility’ is justified in terms of the context, but there is nothing in the word ταπεινοφροσύνη itself which means ‘false.’ It would be possible to render ταπεινοφροσύνη in [COL 2:18](https://ref.ly/Phil2:18) as ‘subjection to,’ and one might render the entire expression as ‘in abject worship of angels.’ In other languages ‘false humility’ may be rendered as ‘just pretending to be humble’ or ‘appearing to be humble but really being proud.’

[ACT 20:19](https://ref.ly/John20:19) · [EPH 4:2](https://ref.ly/Gal4:2) · [PHP 2:3](https://ref.ly/Eph2:3) · [COL 2:18](https://ref.ly/Phil2:18) · [COL 2:23](https://ref.ly/Phil2:23) · [COL 3:12](https://ref.ly/Phil3:12) · [1PE 5:5](https://ref.ly/Jas5:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 20:19; Ephesians 4:2; Philippians 2:3; Colossians 2:18; Colossians 2:23; Colossians 3:12; 1 Peter 5:5

## ταπεινόω (id: 004919000000000)

ταπεινόω
========

ταπεινόω (G5013) — ταπεινόομαι

verb \| ταπεινός · ταπεινοφροσύνη · ταπεινόφρων · ταπείνωσις

81\.7 · Spacial Dimensions · High, Low, Deep

to make low to cause something to become low in height For another (probably preferred) interpretation of [LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5), see [79\.87](#79.87).

[LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5)

79\.87 · Features of Objects · Uneven \[Rough], Level \[Smooth]

to level off, to make level to cause something to become level One might argue that ταπεινόω in [LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5) is to be understood as ‘to be brought low,’ but in contrast with πληρωθήσεται, which refers to filling up valleys, ταπεινωθήσεται should perhaps be understood as referring to ‘leveling off’ mountains and hills. For this other interpretation of ταπεινόω in [LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5), see [81\.7](#81.7).

[LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5)

87\.62 · Status · Low Status or Rank \[including persons of low status]

to make humble, to bring down low to cause someone to be in a low status

[MAT 23:12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:12) · [2CO 11:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:7) · [PHP 2:8](https://ref.ly/Eph2:8) · [JAS 4:10](https://ref.ly/Heb4:10)

88\.56 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Humility

to make humble, to humble (derivative of ταπεινός\[b] ‘humble,’ [88\.52](#88.52)) to cause someone to be or to become humble A strictly literal rendering of ‘he who humbles himself’ could be misunderstood as ‘one who despises himself’ or ‘one who has no regard for himself.’ In the context of [MAT 18:4](https://ref.ly/Matt18:4) it is often important to use an idiomatic expression which will adequately convey the meaning, for example, ‘one who causes his heart to bow down’ or even ‘one who makes his heart small.’

[MAT 18:4](https://ref.ly/Matt18:4) · [MAT 23:12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:12) · [JAS 4:10](https://ref.ly/Heb4:10) · [1PE 5:6](https://ref.ly/Jas5:6)

25\.198 · Attitudes and Emotions · Shame, Disgrace, Humiliation

to humiliate, to put to shame to cause someone to become disgraced and humiliated, with the implication of embarrassment and shame

[MAT 23:12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:12) · [MAT 23:12](https://ref.ly/Matt23:12) · [2CO 12:21](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:21)

87\.63 · (ταπεινόομαι) · Status · Low Status or Rank \[including persons of low status]

to live in humble circumstances, to live like those of low status to live in circumstances regarded as characteristic of low status In a number of languages ταπεινόομαι in [PHP 4:12](https://ref.ly/Eph4:12) may be rendered as ‘to live like poor people.’

[LUK 3:5](https://ref.ly/Mark3:5) · [LUK 14:11](https://ref.ly/Mark14:11) · [LUK 14:11](https://ref.ly/Mark14:11) · [LUK 18:14](https://ref.ly/Mark18:14) · [LUK 18:14](https://ref.ly/Mark18:14) · [PHP 4:12](https://ref.ly/Eph4:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 3:5; Matthew 23:12; 2 Corinthians 11:7; Philippians 2:8; James 4:10; Matthew 18:4; 1 Peter 5:6; 2 Corinthians 12:21; Luke 14:11; Luke 18:14; Philippians 4:12


## ταπείνωσις (id: 004920000000000)

ταπείνωσις
==========

ταπείνωσις (G5014)

noun, f. \| \-εως \| ταπεινόω

88\.51 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Humility

humility, humble behavior the quality of unpretentious behavior, suggesting a total lack of arrogance or pride In some languages humility is expressed indirectly by an idiomatic phrase, for example, ‘to live without strutting’ or ‘to walk without wanting to be noticed.’

[JAS 1:10](https://ref.ly/Heb1:10)

87\.60 · Status · Low Status or Rank \[including persons of low status]

low status, low estate, humility the state of low status, with the probable implication of humility

[LUK 1:48](https://ref.ly/Mark1:48) · [ACT 8:33](https://ref.ly/John8:33) · [PHP 3:21](https://ref.ly/Eph3:21) · [JAS 1:10](https://ref.ly/Heb1:10)

* **Associated Passages:** James 1:10; Luke 1:48; Acts 8:33; Philippians 3:21


## ταράσσω (id: 004921000000000)

ταράσσω
=======

ταράσσω (G5015)

verb \| pf.pass. τετάραγμαι · 3sg. τετάρακται · aor.pass. ἐταράχθην · subj. ταραχθῶ \| διαταράσσομαι · ἐκταράσσω · ταραχή · τάραχος

16\.3 · Non\-Linear Movement

to cause to move, to stir up to cause movement, usually as the result of shaking or stirring This word is found as a variant reading only: ἄγγελος γὰρ κυρίου κατὰ καιρὸν κατέβαινεν ἐν τῇ κολυμβήθρᾳ καὶ ἐταράσσετο τὸ ὕδωρ ‘from time to time an angel of the Lord would come down in the pool and cause the water to move’ [JHN 5:4](https://ref.ly/Luke5:4) (apparatus).

[JHN 5:7](https://ref.ly/Luke5:7)

25\.244 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

to cause great mental distress (a figurative extension of meaning of ταράσσω\[a] ‘to stir up,’ [16\.3](#16.3)) to cause acute emotional distress or turbulence

[MAT 2:3](https://ref.ly/Matt2:3) · [MAT 14:26](https://ref.ly/Matt14:26) · [MRK 6:50](https://ref.ly/Matt6:50) · [LUK 1:12](https://ref.ly/Mark1:12) · [LUK 24:38](https://ref.ly/Mark24:38) · [JHN 11:33](https://ref.ly/Luke11:33) · [JHN 12:27](https://ref.ly/Luke12:27) · [JHN 13:21](https://ref.ly/Luke13:21) · [JHN 14:1](https://ref.ly/Luke14:1) · [JHN 14:27](https://ref.ly/Luke14:27) · [ACT 15:24](https://ref.ly/John15:24) · [GAL 1:7](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:7) · [GAL 5:10](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:10) · [1PE 3:14](https://ref.ly/Jas3:14)

39\.44 · Hostility, Strife · Riot

to stir up against, to start a riot, to cause an uproar to cause people to riot against

[ACT 17:8](https://ref.ly/John17:8) · [ACT 17:13](https://ref.ly/John17:13)

* **Associated Passages:** John 5:7; Matthew 2:3; Matthew 14:26; Mark 6:50; Luke 1:12; Luke 24:38; John 11:33; John 12:27; John 13:21; John 14:1; John 14:27; Acts 15:24; Galatians 1:7; Galatians 5:10; 1 Peter 3:14; Acts 17:8; Acts 17:13


## ταραχή (id: 004922000000000)

ταραχή
======

ταραχή

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| ταράσσω

16\.4 · Non\-Linear Movement

movement, motion the motion resulting from a mass being stirred up or shaken This word is found as a variant reading only: ὁ οὖν πρῶτος ἐμβὰς μετὰ τὴν ταραχὴν τοῦ ὕδατος ὑγιὴς ἐγίνετο ‘the first person to go into (the pool) after the water had been moved was healed’ [JHN 5:4](https://ref.ly/Luke5:4) (apparatus).

[JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3)

39\.42 · Hostility, Strife · Riot

riot disorderly behavior of people in violent opposition to authority This word is found as a variant reading only: λιμοὶ καὶ ταραχαί ‘famines and riots’ [MRK 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8) (apparatus).

[MRK 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8)

* **Associated Passages:** John 5:3; Mark 13:8


## τάραχος (id: 004923000000000)

τάραχος
=======

τάραχος (G5017)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| ταράσσω

39\.5 · Hostility, Strife · Opposition, Hostility

commotion, serious trouble a serious disturbance

[ACT 19:23](https://ref.ly/John19:23)

25\.243 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

great distress, extreme anxiety a state of acute distress and great anxiety, with the additional possible implications of dismay and confusion Since τάραχος refers to the type of extreme anxiety which borders on fear, it may be possible in some languages to use a double expression, ‘were greatly distressed and afraid.’

[ACT 12:18](https://ref.ly/John12:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 19:23; Acts 12:18

[ACT 9:11](https://ref.ly/John9:11) · [ACT 21:39](https://ref.ly/John21:39)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 9:11; Acts 21:39

Tarsus the capital of Cilicia in southeast Asia Minor

[ACT 9:30](https://ref.ly/John9:30) · [ACT 11:25](https://ref.ly/John11:25) · [ACT 22:3](https://ref.ly/John22:3)

## ταρταρόω (id: 004926000000000)

ταρταρόω
========

ταρταρόω (G5020)

verb

1\.25 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Below the Surface of the Earth

to hold in Tartarus, to cast into hell (derivative of τάρταρος ‘Tartarus,’ ‘hell,’ as a place of torture or torment, not occurring in the NT) to cast into or to cause to remain in Tartarus In many cases it is confusing to add still another term for a designation of hell by transliterating the Greek τάρταρος, and so most translators have preferred to render ταρταρόω as either ‘to cast into hell’ or ‘to keep in hell,’ thus using for ‘hell’ the same term as is employed for a rendering of the Greek term γέεννα ([1\.21](#1.21)).

[2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 2:4


## τάσσω (id: 004927000000000)

τάσσω
=====

τάσσω (G5021)

verb \| pf.inf. τεταχέναι · pf.pass. τέταγμαι · 3sg. τέτακται \| ἀνατάσσομαι · ἀντιτάσσομαι · ἀνυπότακτος · ἀποτάσσομαι · ἀτακτέω · ἄτακτος · ἀτάκτως · διαταγή · διάταγμα · διατάσσω · ἐπιδιατάσσομαι · ἐπιταγή · ἐπιτάσσω · προστάσσω · συντάσσω · τάγμα · τακτός · τάξις · ὑποταγή · ὑποτάσσω

37\.96 · Control, Rule · Assign to a Role or Function

to appoint, to designate, to assign, to give a task to to assign someone to a particular task, function, or role Though τάσσω in [ACT 13:48](https://ref.ly/John13:48) has sometimes been interpreted as meaning ‘to choose,’ there seems to be far more involved than merely a matter of selection, since a relationship is specifically assigned.

[ACT 13:48](https://ref.ly/John13:48) · [ACT 15:2](https://ref.ly/John15:2) · [ACT 22:10](https://ref.ly/John22:10) · [ROM 13:1](https://ref.ly/Acts13:1)

13\.13 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to cause to be, to be placed to cause someone to be in a state involving an order or arrangement

[LUK 7:8](https://ref.ly/Mark7:8)

33\.325 · Communication · Command, Order

to order, to instruct, to tell, to command to give detailed instructions as to what must be done1

[MAT 28:16](https://ref.ly/Matt28:16)

33\.346 · Communication · Recommend, Propose

to propose, to suggest to propose something to someone It is also possible to understand τάσσω in [ACT 28:23](https://ref.ly/John28:23) as meaning ‘to arrange,’ but in [ACT 28:23](https://ref.ly/John28:23) it would seem that τάσσω implies not only proposing a date but obtaining an agreement.

[ACT 28:23](https://ref.ly/John28:23)

68\.69 · Aspect · Do Intensely or Extensively

to do with devotion, to give oneself to to do something with devotion, with the possible implication of systematic, regular activity

[1CO 16:15](https://ref.ly/Rom16:15)

1 The meanings of τάσσω\[c], συντάσσω, προστάσσω\[a], ἐπιτάσσω, and διατάσσω\[a] no doubt differ somewhat, particularly in connotation, but it is not possible to determine this from existing contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 13:48; Acts 15:2; Acts 22:10; Romans 13:1; Luke 7:8; Matthew 28:16; Acts 28:23; 1 Corinthians 16:15


## ταῦρος (id: 004928000000000)

ταῦρος
======

ταῦρος (G5022)

noun, m. \| \-ου

4\.16 · Animals · Animals

bull male bovine; large ruminant animal with horns and cloven hoofs; used for sacrifice and for meat, as a beast of burden, or for pulling a cart or a plow In a number of languages the equivalent of ‘bull’ is simply a generic term for cattle to which is added a specific designation such as ‘male.’

[MAT 22:4](https://ref.ly/Matt22:4) · [ACT 14:13](https://ref.ly/John14:13) · [HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13) · [HEB 10:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 22:4; Acts 14:13; Hebrews 9:13; Hebrews 10:4


## ταφή (id: 004929000000000)

ταφή
====

ταφή (G5027)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| θάπτω

52\.9 · Funerals and Burial

burial place a place for burying It is also possible to understand ταφή in the context of [MAT 27:7](https://ref.ly/Matt27:7) as a reference to the process of burial, and one may therefore translate [MAT 27:7](https://ref.ly/Matt27:7) as ‘they used the money to buy the Potter’s Field to bury foreigners.’

[MAT 27:7](https://ref.ly/Matt27:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:7


## τάφος (id: 004930000000000)

τάφος
=====

τάφος (G5028)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| θάπτω

7\.75 · Constructions · Miscellaneous Constructions

grave, tomb a construction for the burial of the dead; often a natural cave or hewn out of bedrock1 In a number of languages it is important to distinguish clearly between a grave (a hole in the ground in which a corpse is placed) and a tomb (a construction built above the surface of the ground for housing a corpse). In some contexts, however, it may be better to use a more generic expression, for example, ‘places where people are buried’ or ‘places where corpses are placed.’ In [MRK 5:2](https://ref.ly/Matt5:2) it is important to avoid a term which would designate merely graves, for the demoniac who met Jesus was not living down in graves in the ground, but had found some habitation either in burial caves or in tombs constructed above ground.

[MAT 23:27](https://ref.ly/Matt23:27) · [MAT 23:29](https://ref.ly/Matt23:29) · [MAT 27:61](https://ref.ly/Matt27:61) · [MAT 27:64](https://ref.ly/Matt27:64) · [MAT 27:66](https://ref.ly/Matt27:66) · [MAT 28:1](https://ref.ly/Matt28:1) · [ROM 3:13](https://ref.ly/Acts3:13)

1 It is possible that μνῆμα and μνημεῖον\[a] differ in meaning from τάφος in that they contain a semantic component of memorial, that is, a reminder to people of someone who has died.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 23:27; Matthew 23:29; Matthew 27:61; Matthew 27:64; Matthew 27:66; Matthew 28:1; Romans 3:13

67\.110 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

quickly, hurriedly, swift, speedy pertaining to a very short extent of time In [GAL 1:6](https://ref.ly/2Cor1:6) ταχέως refers clearly to the relatively brief period of time before the Galatians abandoned their earlier convictions.

## ταχύς (id: 004935000000000)

ταχύς
=====

ταχύς (G5035) — ταχύ

adjc. \| \-εῖα, \-ύ \| τάχα · ταχέως · ταχινός · τάχιον · τάχιστα · τάχος · ταχύ

67\.110 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

quickly, hurriedly, swift, speedy pertaining to a very short extent of time In [JHN 11:29](https://ref.ly/Luke11:29) ταχύ probably refers to the short period of time between Mary‘s hearing about Jesus and her getting up to go out to meet him. It is, of course, also possible to interpret ταχύ in [JHN 11:29](https://ref.ly/Luke11:29) as referring to the rapidity of Mary‘s movement in getting up and going out to meet Jesus.  
Again, in [JHN 13:27](https://ref.ly/Luke13:27) the emphasis is upon the brief period of time before Judas is to do what he had set out to do.

## τεῖχος (id: 004937000000000)

τεῖχος
======

τεῖχος (G5038)

noun, n. \| \-ους \| τοῖχος

7\.61 · Constructions · Walls and Fences

city wall a particularly strong permanent wall, primarily the wall built around a city for its protection In a number of languages a translator must make a clear distinction between a wall of a house and a city wall. The wall of a house may be called ‘a side of a house’ and an inner wall ‘a partition in a house,’ while a city wall is often related to terms such as ‘barricade’ or ‘fence.’ Hence, a city wall may be called ‘a fortified fence around a city.’

[ACT 9:25](https://ref.ly/John9:25) · [2CO 11:33](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:33) · [HEB 11:30](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:30) · [REV 21:12](https://ref.ly/Jude21:12) · [REV 21:14](https://ref.ly/Jude21:14) · [REV 21:15](https://ref.ly/Jude21:15) · [REV 21:17](https://ref.ly/Jude21:17) · [REV 21:18](https://ref.ly/Jude21:18) · [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 9:25; 2 Corinthians 11:33; Hebrews 11:30; Revelation 21:12; Revelation 21:14; Revelation 21:15; Revelation 21:17; Revelation 21:18; Revelation 21:19


## τεκμήριον (id: 004938000000000)

τεκμήριον
=========

τεκμήριον (G5039)

noun, n. \| \-ου

28\.45 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

evidence, proof, convincing proof that which causes something to be known as verified or confirmed In a number of languages ‘convincing proof’ is rendered as ‘that which causes one to know for sure’ or ‘... with certainty.’

[ACT 1:3](https://ref.ly/John1:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 1:3


## τεκνίον (id: 004939000000000)

τεκνίον
=======

τεκνίον (G5040)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| τίκτω

9\.46 · People · Persons For Whom There Is Affectionate Concern

my child, my dear friend, my dear man, my dear one, my dear lad (extension of meaning of τέκνον\[a] ‘child, offspring,’ [10\.36](#10.36)) a person of any age for whom there is a special relationship of endearment and association It may be impossible to translate τεκνία literally as ‘my children’ in [1JN 3:7](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:7) since this might suggest a kinship relationship between the author of 1 John and the people to whom he is addressing his letter. A more satisfactory equivalent in some languages is often ‘my dear friends’ or ‘my dear ones.’

[JHN 13:33](https://ref.ly/Luke13:33) · [1JN 2:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:1) · [1JN 2:12](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:12) · [1JN 2:28](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:28) · [1JN 3:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:18) · [1JN 4:4](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:4) · [1JN 5:21](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:21)

* **Associated Passages:** John 13:33; 1 John 2:1; 1 John 2:12; 1 John 2:28; 1 John 3:18; 1 John 4:4; 1 John 5:21


## τεκνογονέω (id: 004940000000000)

τεκνογονέω
==========

τεκνογονέω (G5041)

verb \| τίκτω \+ γίνομαι

23\.52 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

to bear, to give birth to give birth to a child1 All languages have expressions for human birth, though these are frequently in idiomatic forms, for example, ‘to drop a child’ or ‘to cause a baby to pass between the legs.’ A number of languages have a variety of terms referring to giving birth, and some of these may involve unfortunate connotations. One must therefore be careful about the selection of appropriate expressions.

[1TI 5:14](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:14)

1 It is possible that τεκνογονέω and τεκνογονία differ somewhat in connotation from τίκτω\[a] and γεννάω\[b] in being stylistically more formal, but there seems to be no significant denotative distinction in meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 5:14

23\.52 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

One must therefore be careful about the selection of appropriate expressions.

## τέκνον (id: 004942000000000)

τέκνον
======

τέκνον (G5043)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| τίκτω

10\.36 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

child, offspring one’s immediate offspring, but without specific reference to sex or age In languages in which there is no generic term for ‘child’ or ‘offspring,’ one may use ‘son’ or ‘daughter’ or ‘son and daughter,’ singular or plural, depending upon the context.

[MAT 2:18](https://ref.ly/Matt2:18) · [MAT 7:11](https://ref.ly/Matt7:11) · [MAT 10:21](https://ref.ly/Matt10:21) · [MAT 10:21](https://ref.ly/Matt10:21) · [MAT 15:26](https://ref.ly/Matt15:26) · [MAT 18:25](https://ref.ly/Matt18:25) · [MAT 19:29](https://ref.ly/Matt19:29) · [MAT 21:28](https://ref.ly/Matt21:28) · [MAT 21:28](https://ref.ly/Matt21:28) · [MAT 22:24](https://ref.ly/Matt22:24) · [MRK 7:27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:27) · [MRK 7:27](https://ref.ly/Matt7:27) · [MRK 10:29](https://ref.ly/Matt10:29) · [MRK 10:30](https://ref.ly/Matt10:30) · [MRK 12:19](https://ref.ly/Matt12:19) · [MRK 13:12](https://ref.ly/Matt13:12) · [MRK 13:12](https://ref.ly/Matt13:12) · [LUK 1:7](https://ref.ly/Mark1:7) · [LUK 1:17](https://ref.ly/Mark1:17) · [LUK 2:48](https://ref.ly/Mark2:48) · [LUK 11:13](https://ref.ly/Mark11:13) · [LUK 14:26](https://ref.ly/Mark14:26) · [LUK 15:31](https://ref.ly/Mark15:31) · [LUK 18:29](https://ref.ly/Mark18:29) · [LUK 20:31](https://ref.ly/Mark20:31) · [LUK 23:28](https://ref.ly/Mark23:28) · [ACT 7:5](https://ref.ly/John7:5) · [ACT 21:5](https://ref.ly/John21:5) · [ACT 21:21](https://ref.ly/John21:21) · [1CO 7:14](https://ref.ly/Rom7:14) · [2CO 12:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:14) · [2CO 12:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:14) · [GAL 4:27](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:27) · [EPH 6:1](https://ref.ly/Gal6:1) · [EPH 6:4](https://ref.ly/Gal6:4) · [PHP 2:22](https://ref.ly/Eph2:22) · [COL 3:20](https://ref.ly/Phil3:20) · [COL 3:21](https://ref.ly/Phil3:21) · [1TH 2:7](https://ref.ly/Col2:7) · [1TH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Col2:11) · [1TI 3:4](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:4) · [1TI 3:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:12) · [1TI 5:4](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:4) · [TIT 1:6](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:6) · [1JN 3:1](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:1) · [1JN 3:2](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:2) · [2JN 1:1](https://ref.ly/1John1:1) · [2JN 1:4](https://ref.ly/1John1:4) · [2JN 1:13](https://ref.ly/1John1:13) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4) · [REV 12:5](https://ref.ly/Jude12:5)

10\.28 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

posterity, descendants, offspring successive following generations of those who are biologically related to a reference person In the case of γενεά\[c], τέκνον\[b], and σπέρμα\[b] ([10\.29](#10.29)), the reference is not to one’s immediate descendants or offspring (that is to say, to one’s sons or daughters) but to a successive series of such persons, one’s descendants. In some languages such descendants may be called merely ‘the children of one’s children,’ and in other languages one may refer to descendants as ‘those who follow one’ or ‘those who come later.’

[MAT 3:9](https://ref.ly/Matt3:9) · [MAT 27:25](https://ref.ly/Matt27:25) · [LUK 3:8](https://ref.ly/Mark3:8) · [LUK 16:25](https://ref.ly/Mark16:25) · [JHN 8:39](https://ref.ly/Luke8:39) · [ACT 2:39](https://ref.ly/John2:39) · [ACT 13:33](https://ref.ly/John13:33) · [ROM 9:8](https://ref.ly/Acts9:8) · [1PE 3:6](https://ref.ly/Jas3:6)

11\.63 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

persons of, people of (a figurative extension of meaning of τέκνον\[a] ‘child,’ [10\.36](#10.36)) inhabitants of a particular place Only rarely can one preserve the figurative significance of τέκνον\[c] as a designation of the inhabitants of an area. Readers are too likely to understand such a reference as applicable only to children who live in a particular place. Even the use of a simile does not assist appreciably, since it would be interpreted as likening the inhabitants of an area to children, probably in the sense of their being immature or incapable. For example, the expression the people of Jerusalem like children would probably lead to serious misunderstanding.

[MAT 23:37](https://ref.ly/Matt23:37) · [LUK 13:34](https://ref.ly/Mark13:34) · [LUK 19:44](https://ref.ly/Mark19:44)

9\.46 · People · Persons For Whom There Is Affectionate Concern

my child, my dear friend, my dear man, my dear one, my dear lad (extension of meaning of τέκνον\[a] ‘child, offspring,’ [10\.36](#10.36)) a person of any age for whom there is a special relationship of endearment and association In a number of languages it is impossible to translate τέκνον in [MAT 9:2](https://ref.ly/Matt9:2) as ‘child,’ since this might immediately suggest that Jesus was declaring himself to be the father of this man. Furthermore, the paralytic was evidently an adult male. A more satisfactory equivalent would be ‘my dear man’ or ‘my dear fellow.’

[MAT 9:2](https://ref.ly/Matt9:2) · [MRK 2:5](https://ref.ly/Matt2:5) · [MRK 10:24](https://ref.ly/Matt10:24) · [1CO 4:14](https://ref.ly/Rom4:14) · [1CO 4:17](https://ref.ly/Rom4:17) · [2CO 6:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:13) · [GAL 4:19](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:19) · [EPH 5:1](https://ref.ly/Gal5:1) · [1TI 1:18](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:18) · [2TI 1:2](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:2) · [2TI 2:1](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:1) · [TIT 1:4](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:4)

36\.40 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Follow, Be a Disciple

disciple a person who looks to another as being, so to speak, a father in the faith and thus becomes a disciple of that person It is also possible that τέκνον in [3JN 1:4](https://ref.ly/2John1:4) is to be understood simply as an affectionate way of talking about persons who in one way or another are in a dependent relationship to someone (see [9\.46](#9.46)).

[ROM 9:7](https://ref.ly/Acts9:7) · [1TI 1:2](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:2) · [TIT 1:4](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:4) · [PHM 1:10](https://ref.ly/Titus1:10) · [3JN 1:4](https://ref.ly/2John1:4) · [REV 2:23](https://ref.ly/Jude2:23)

58\.26 · Nature, Class, Example · Class, Kind

son of, offspring of, child of, kind of, one who has the characteristics of, person of a kind or class of persons, with the implication of possessing certain derived characteristics

[LUK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Mark7:35) · [JHN 1:12](https://ref.ly/Luke1:12) · [JHN 11:52](https://ref.ly/Luke11:52) · [ROM 8:16](https://ref.ly/Acts8:16) · [ROM 8:17](https://ref.ly/Acts8:17) · [ROM 8:21](https://ref.ly/Acts8:21) · [ROM 9:8](https://ref.ly/Acts9:8) · [ROM 9:8](https://ref.ly/Acts9:8) · [GAL 4:25](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:25) · [GAL 4:28](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:28) · [GAL 4:31](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:31) · [EPH 2:3](https://ref.ly/Gal2:3) · [PHP 2:15](https://ref.ly/Eph2:15) · [1PE 1:14](https://ref.ly/Jas1:14) · [2PE 2:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:14) · [1JN 3:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:10) · [1JN 3:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:10) · [1JN 5:2](https://ref.ly/2Pet5:2)

11\.14 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

**Collocation:** τέκνα φωτός

sons of the light, children of the light, people of God (an idiom, literally: children of light) persons to whom the truth of God has been revealed and who are presumably living according to such truth. See also [9\.4](#9.4) and [12\.15](#12.15) In a number of languages it is difficult to speak of ‘light’ in the metaphorical sense of the truth that comes from God. Such truth is not to be equated with knowledge, but with the principles and practices of right moral behavior. Because of these difficulties in speaking of ‘truth’ as ‘light,’ a number of translators have preferred to use the expression ‘people of God’ for the phrases υἱοὶ τοῦ φωτός, υἱοὶ τῆς ἡμέρας, and τέκνα φωτός. In some instances, however, it is possible to employ ‘light,’ if this is described as ‘light that comes from God’ or even ‘the true light from God.’

[EPH 5:8](https://ref.ly/Gal5:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 2:18; Matthew 7:11; Matthew 10:21; Matthew 15:26; Matthew 18:25; Matthew 19:29; Matthew 21:28; Matthew 22:24; Mark 7:27; Mark 10:29; Mark 10:30; Mark 12:19; Mark 13:12; Luke 1:7; Luke 1:17; Luke 2:48; Luke 11:13; Luke 14:26; Luke 15:31; Luke 18:29; Luke 20:31; Luke 23:28; Acts 7:5; Acts 21:5; Acts 21:21; 1 Corinthians 7:14; 2 Corinthians 12:14; Galatians 4:27; Ephesians 6:1; Ephesians 6:4; Philippians 2:22; Colossians 3:20; Colossians 3:21; 1 Thessalonians 2:7; 1 Thessalonians 2:11; 1 Timothy 3:4; 1 Timothy 3:12; 1 Timothy 5:4; Titus 1:6; 1 John 3:1; 1 John 3:2; 2 John 1:1; 2 John 1:4; 2 John 1:13; Revelation 12:4; Revelation 12:5; Matthew 3:9; Matthew 27:25; Luke 3:8; Luke 16:25; John 8:39; Acts 2:39; Acts 13:33; Romans 9:8; 1 Peter 3:6; Matthew 23:37; Luke 13:34; Luke 19:44; Matthew 9:2; Mark 2:5; Mark 10:24; 1 Corinthians 4:14; 1 Corinthians 4:17; 2 Corinthians 6:13; Galatians 4:19; Ephesians 5:1; 1 Timothy 1:18; 2 Timothy 1:2; 2 Timothy 2:1; Titus 1:4; Romans 9:7; 1 Timothy 1:2; Philemon 1:10; 3 John 1:4; Revelation 2:23; Luke 7:35; John 1:12; John 11:52; Romans 8:16; Romans 8:17; Romans 8:21; Galatians 4:25; Galatians 4:28; Galatians 4:31; Ephesians 2:3; Philippians 2:15; 1 Peter 1:14; 2 Peter 2:14; 1 John 3:10; 1 John 5:2; Ephesians 5:8


## τεκνοτροφέω (id: 004943000000000)

τεκνοτροφέω
===========

τεκνοτροφέω (G5044)

verb \| τίκτω \+ τρέφω

35\.51 · Help, Care For · Rear, Bring Up

to raise, to rear, to bring up to raise a child to maturity by providing for physical and psychological needs1 To raise or bring up children may be expressed in a number of different ways, for example, ‘to give food to children,’ ‘to take care of children,’ ‘to be a parent to children,’ ‘to cause a child to become an adult,’ or ‘to make a child become like oneself.’

[1TI 5:10](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:10)

1 There may very well be subtle differences of meaning in the series in [35\.51](#35.51), but there is no direct contextual evidence to support significant distinctions in meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 5:10

45\.9 · Building, Constructing

builder, carpenter one who uses various materials (wood, stone, and metal) in building There is every reason to believe that in biblical times one who was regarded as a τέκτων would be skilled in the use of wood and stone and possibly even metal.

## τέλειος (id: 004945000000000)

τέλειος
=======

τέλειος (G5046)

adjc. \| \-α, \-ον \| τελέω

88\.36 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Perfect, Perfection

perfect pertaining to being perfect in the sense of not lacking any moral quality Compare the meaning of τέλειος\[e] mature in [88\.100](#88.100).

[MAT 5:48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:48) · [MAT 5:48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:48) · [MAT 19:21](https://ref.ly/Matt19:21) · [ROM 12:2](https://ref.ly/Acts12:2) · [JAS 1:4](https://ref.ly/Heb1:4) · [JAS 1:17](https://ref.ly/Heb1:17) · [JAS 1:25](https://ref.ly/Heb1:25) · [JAS 3:2](https://ref.ly/Heb3:2)

73\.6 · Genuine, Phony

genuine, true pertaining to being truly and completely genuine

[1JN 4:18](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:18)

79\.129 · Features of Objects · Perfect

perfect pertaining to having no defect whatsoever

[HEB 9:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:11) · [JAS 1:17](https://ref.ly/Heb1:17)

68\.23 · Aspect · Complete, Finish, Succeed

complete, finished pertaining to that which is fully accomplished or finished

[1CO 13:10](https://ref.ly/Rom13:10) · [JAS 1:4](https://ref.ly/Heb1:4)

88\.100 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Mature Behavior

mature, grown\-up pertaining to being mature in one’s behavior It is also possible to interpret τέλειος in [EPH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gal4:13) as meaning ‘perfect’ (see [88\.36](#88.36)).  
In [MAT 5:48](https://ref.ly/Matt5:48) it is possible that τέλειος also means maturity of behavior, but it is usually interpreted as ‘being perfect,’ since the comparison is made with God (see [88\.36](#88.36)).

[1CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/Rom2:6) · [1CO 13:10](https://ref.ly/Rom13:10) · [1CO 14:20](https://ref.ly/Rom14:20) · [EPH 4:13](https://ref.ly/Gal4:13) · [COL 1:28](https://ref.ly/Phil1:28) · [COL 4:12](https://ref.ly/Phil4:12) · [HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14) · [JAS 1:4](https://ref.ly/Heb1:4) · [JAS 3:2](https://ref.ly/Heb3:2)

9\.10 · People · Human Beings

grown person, adult pertaining to an adult human being Though in [HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14) τέλειος is to be understood in a literal sense, the context as a whole is figurative.

[1CO 14:20](https://ref.ly/Rom14:20) · [HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14)

11\.18 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

initiated one who is initiated into a religious community of faith (a meaning which reflects the occurrence of τέλειος as a technical term for persons initiated into the mystery religions) In a number of languages ‘initiated’ ([PHP 3:15](https://ref.ly/Eph3:15) [COL 1:28](https://ref.ly/Phil1:28)) may be best expressed as ‘to become a member of’ or ‘to become a believer in.’ It is possible, however, to interpret τέλειος in [PHP 3:15](https://ref.ly/Eph3:15) and [COL 1:28](https://ref.ly/Phil1:28) as mature spirituality or a state of being spiritually mature (see [88\.100](#88.100)).

[PHP 3:15](https://ref.ly/Eph3:15) · [COL 1:28](https://ref.ly/Phil1:28)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:48; Matthew 19:21; Romans 12:2; James 1:4; James 1:17; James 1:25; James 3:2; 1 John 4:18; Hebrews 9:11; 1 Corinthians 13:10; 1 Corinthians 2:6; 1 Corinthians 14:20; Ephesians 4:13; Colossians 1:28; Colossians 4:12; Hebrews 5:14; Philippians 3:15

68\.22 · Aspect · Complete, Finish, Succeed

to complete, to finish, to end, to accomplish to bring an activity to a successful finish1

53\.50 · Religious Activities · Dedicate, Consecrate

to admit into, to initiate to admit into or initiate into faith (possibly based on technical usage in the mystery religions) It is important that in [PHP 3:12](https://ref.ly/Eph3:12) τελειόω is to be understood in the sense of a functional stage of religious attainment: ‘I have already become an initiate.’ For another interpretation of τελειόω in [PHP 3:12](https://ref.ly/Eph3:12), see [68\.31](#68.31).

[PHP 3:12](https://ref.ly/Eph3:12)

13\.126 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Happen

to make happen, to fulfill, to bring to fruition, to accomplish, fulfillment to cause to happen for some end result

[JHN 19:28](https://ref.ly/Luke19:28)

13\.18 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to attain, to become to attain a state as a goal

[JHN 17:23](https://ref.ly/Luke17:23)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions, particularly of emphasis, in the series τελέω, ἐκτελέω\[a], ἀποτελέω, ἐπιτελέω\[a], συντελέω\[a], and τελειόω\[c], but it is not possible to determine with precision the particular distinctions on the basis of existing contexts, though possibly ἐκτελέω and ἀποτελέω emphasize more finality, while ἐπιτελέω\[a] may focus upon the resulting purpose.

## τέλος (id: 004955000000000)

τέλος
=====

τέλος (G5056)

noun, n. \| \-ους \| τελέω

67\.66 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Duration of Time: Beginning, End

end a point of time marking the end of a duration There are serious problems involved in rendering τέλος\[a] in [MAT 24:14](https://ref.ly/Matt24:14) and in similar contexts. In a number of languages one simply cannot say ‘the end will come’; rather, it may be necessary to say ‘that is the finish’ or ‘everything is finished.’ In the context of [MAT 24:14](https://ref.ly/Matt24:14), however, it may be best to translate ‘God will finish everything.’ The phrase εἰς τέλος in [1TH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Col2:16) may also be understood as an idiomatic expression involving a degree of completeness (see [78\.47](#78.47)).

[MAT 10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22) · [MAT 24:6](https://ref.ly/Matt24:6) · [MAT 24:13](https://ref.ly/Matt24:13) · [MAT 24:14](https://ref.ly/Matt24:14) · [MRK 3:26](https://ref.ly/Matt3:26) · [MRK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Matt13:7) · [MRK 13:13](https://ref.ly/Matt13:13) · [LUK 1:33](https://ref.ly/Mark1:33) · [LUK 21:9](https://ref.ly/Mark21:9) · [LUK 22:37](https://ref.ly/Mark22:37) · [ROM 10:4](https://ref.ly/Acts10:4) · [1CO 1:8](https://ref.ly/Rom1:8) · [1CO 10:11](https://ref.ly/Rom10:11) · [2CO 3:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:13) · [2CO 11:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:15) · [1TH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Col2:16) · [HEB 3:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:14) · [HEB 6:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:8) · [HEB 6:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:11) · [HEB 7:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:3) · [1PE 4:7](https://ref.ly/Jas4:7) · [REV 2:26](https://ref.ly/Jude2:26) · [REV 21:6](https://ref.ly/Jude21:6) · [REV 22:13](https://ref.ly/Jude22:13)

89\.40 · Relations · Result

outcome, result, end the result of an event or process, with special focus upon the final state or condition In some languages τέλος in [MAT 26:58](https://ref.ly/Matt26:58) may be rendered simply as ‘what would happen’ or ‘what would finally happen.’

[MAT 26:58](https://ref.ly/Matt26:58) · [ROM 6:21](https://ref.ly/Acts6:21) · [ROM 6:22](https://ref.ly/Acts6:22) · [PHP 3:19](https://ref.ly/Eph3:19) · [HEB 6:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:8) · [JAS 5:11](https://ref.ly/Heb5:11) · [1PE 1:9](https://ref.ly/Jas1:9) · [1PE 4:17](https://ref.ly/Jas4:17)

89\.55 · Relations · Purpose

purpose, intent, goal the purpose of an event or state, viewed in terms of its result

[ROM 10:4](https://ref.ly/Acts10:4) · [1TI 1:5](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:5) · [1PE 1:9](https://ref.ly/Jas1:9)

78\.47 · Degree · Completely, Enough \[Completive Degree]

**Collocation:** εἰς τέλος

completely, totally, entirely, wholly a degree of completeness, with the possible implication of purpose or result It is also possible to understand the phrase ἕως τέλους in the temporal sense of ‘to the end’ (see [67\.66](#67.66)).  
It is also possible to understand τέλος in the expression εἰς τέλος in [1TH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Col2:16) as a temporal expression, with εἰς ([67\.117](#67.117)) as a marker of an extent of time, so that this passage may be rendered as ‘and in the end wrath has come down on them’ or ‘and wrath has at last come down on them’ (see [67\.66](#67.66)). In this context ὀργή may very well be translated as ‘punishment’ ([38\.10](#38.10)), and in many languages it is necessary to indicate the agent of such punishment. The same ambiguity with εἰς τέλος occurs in [JHN 13:1](https://ref.ly/Luke13:1) in the clause εἰς τέλος ἠγάπησεν αὐτούς, meaning ‘he loved them completely’ or ‘he loved them to the end’ (see [67\.119](#67.119)).

[LUK 18:5](https://ref.ly/Mark18:5) · [JHN 13:1](https://ref.ly/Luke13:1) · [2CO 1:13](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:13) · [1TH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Col2:16)

57\.179 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Tax, Tribute

duty, tax, revenue payments customarily due a governmental authority The term τέλος\[e] differs from κῆνσος ([57\.180](#57.180)) in being somewhat more generic in meaning. In certain contexts τέλος\[e] may refer to various kinds of direct taxes, customs duties, and tribute money, but in contexts such as [MAT 17:25](https://ref.ly/Matt17:25) in which κῆνσος also occurs, τέλος probably refers primarily to customs duties, while κῆνσος refers to a direct poll tax upon all adult males.

[MAT 17:25](https://ref.ly/Matt17:25) · [ROM 13:7](https://ref.ly/Acts13:7) · [ROM 13:7](https://ref.ly/Acts13:7)

61\.17 · Sequence

**Collocation:** τὸ τέλος

finally, in conclusion (an idiom, literally: the end) a marker of a conclusion to what has preceded, but not necessarily the conclusion of a text

[1CO 15:24](https://ref.ly/Rom15:24) · [1PE 3:8](https://ref.ly/Jas3:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:22; Matthew 24:6; Matthew 24:13; Matthew 24:14; Mark 3:26; Mark 13:7; Mark 13:13; Luke 1:33; Luke 21:9; Luke 22:37; Romans 10:4; 1 Corinthians 1:8; 1 Corinthians 10:11; 2 Corinthians 3:13; 2 Corinthians 11:15; 1 Thessalonians 2:16; Hebrews 3:14; Hebrews 6:8; Hebrews 6:11; Hebrews 7:3; 1 Peter 4:7; Revelation 2:26; Revelation 21:6; Revelation 22:13; Matthew 26:58; Romans 6:21; Romans 6:22; Philippians 3:19; James 5:11; 1 Peter 1:9; 1 Peter 4:17; 1 Timothy 1:5; Luke 18:5; John 13:1; 2 Corinthians 1:13; Matthew 17:25; Romans 13:7; 1 Corinthians 15:24; 1 Peter 3:8


## τελώνης (id: 004956000000000)

τελώνης
=======

τελώνης (G5057)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| τελέω \+ ὠνέομαι

57\.184 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Tax, Tribute

tax collector, revenue officer (derivative of τελέω\[e] ‘to pay taxes,’ [57\.178](#57.178)) one who collects taxes for the government Since Jews who farmed the taxes for the Romans (that is to say, who paid Roman authorities for the privilege of collecting taxes) were considered traitors to their own people, the term τελώνης has strongly negative connotations in the NT. In any translation of the Gospels it may be especially important to have an adequate marginal note designed to explain the basis for the hostility which many people had toward tax collectors.

[MAT 5:46](https://ref.ly/Matt5:46) · [MAT 9:10](https://ref.ly/Matt9:10) · [MAT 9:11](https://ref.ly/Matt9:11) · [MAT 10:3](https://ref.ly/Matt10:3) · [MAT 11:19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:19) · [MAT 18:17](https://ref.ly/Matt18:17) · [MAT 21:31](https://ref.ly/Matt21:31) · [MAT 21:32](https://ref.ly/Matt21:32) · [MRK 2:15](https://ref.ly/Matt2:15) · [MRK 2:16](https://ref.ly/Matt2:16) · [MRK 2:16](https://ref.ly/Matt2:16) · [LUK 3:12](https://ref.ly/Mark3:12) · [LUK 5:27](https://ref.ly/Mark5:27) · [LUK 5:29](https://ref.ly/Mark5:29) · [LUK 5:30](https://ref.ly/Mark5:30) · [LUK 7:29](https://ref.ly/Mark7:29) · [LUK 7:34](https://ref.ly/Mark7:34) · [LUK 15:1](https://ref.ly/Mark15:1) · [LUK 18:10](https://ref.ly/Mark18:10) · [LUK 18:11](https://ref.ly/Mark18:11) · [LUK 18:13](https://ref.ly/Mark18:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:46; Matthew 9:10; Matthew 9:11; Matthew 10:3; Matthew 11:19; Matthew 18:17; Matthew 21:31; Matthew 21:32; Mark 2:15; Mark 2:16; Luke 3:12; Luke 5:27; Luke 5:29; Luke 5:30; Luke 7:29; Luke 7:34; Luke 15:1; Luke 18:10; Luke 18:11; Luke 18:13


## τελώνιον (id: 004957000000000)

τελώνιον
========

τελώνιον (G5058)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| τελέω \+ ὠνέομαι

57\.183 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Tax, Tribute

revenue office, tax office (derivative of τελέω\[e] ‘to pay taxes,’ [57\.178](#57.178)) a place where taxes or revenue was collected from those entering a town to sell produce In the ancient world taxes were primarily of two types: (1\) a head tax on each individual (which was relatively small) and (2\) revenue or tribute paid for goods and produce brought into an area for sale. The latter was essentially a kind of ‘sales tax,’ but paid by the seller who obviously increased the prices of goods accordingly.

[MAT 9:9](https://ref.ly/Matt9:9) · [MRK 2:14](https://ref.ly/Matt2:14) · [LUK 5:27](https://ref.ly/Mark5:27)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:9; Mark 2:14; Luke 5:27


## τέρας (id: 004958000000000)

τέρας
=====

τέρας (G5059)

noun, n. \| \-ατος

33\.480 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

portent, sign an unusual sign, especially one in the heavens, serving to foretell impending events In ancient times a portent might consist of a particular arrangement of the planets, an unusual display of northern lights, a conspicuous comet, or a cluster of falling stars. For a discussion of σημεῖον ‘sign,’ see [33\.477](#33.477).

[MAT 24:24](https://ref.ly/Matt24:24) · [MRK 13:22](https://ref.ly/Matt13:22) · [JHN 4:48](https://ref.ly/Luke4:48) · [ACT 2:19](https://ref.ly/John2:19) · [ACT 2:22](https://ref.ly/John2:22) · [ACT 2:43](https://ref.ly/John2:43) · [ACT 4:30](https://ref.ly/John4:30) · [ACT 5:12](https://ref.ly/John5:12) · [ACT 6:8](https://ref.ly/John6:8) · [ACT 7:36](https://ref.ly/John7:36) · [ACT 14:3](https://ref.ly/John14:3) · [ACT 15:12](https://ref.ly/John15:12) · [ROM 15:19](https://ref.ly/Acts15:19) · [2CO 12:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:12) · [2TH 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:9) · [HEB 2:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:4)

## τέσσαρες (id: 004961000000000)

τέσσαρες

τέσσαρες (G5064)

adjc. \| τεσσάρων · neut. τέσσαρα \| τεσσεράκοντα · τεσσαρεσκαιδέκατος · τεταρταῖος · τέταρτος · τετρααρχέω · τετραάρχης · τετράγωνος · τετράδιον · τετρακισχίλιοι · τετρακόσιοι · τετράμηνος · τετραπλοῦς · τετράπουν · τράπεζα · τραπεζίτης

60\.13 · Number · One, Two, Three, Etc. \[Cardinals]

60\.27 · Number · One, Two, Three, Etc. \[Cardinals]

forty cardinal number, where there are forty instances of a countable entity

[JHN 2:20](https://ref.ly/Luke2:20) · [ACT 4:22](https://ref.ly/John4:22) · [ACT 7:30](https://ref.ly/John7:30) · [ACT 7:42](https://ref.ly/John7:42) · [ACT 23:13](https://ref.ly/John23:13) · [ACT 23:21](https://ref.ly/John23:21) · [2CO 11:24](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:24) · [REV 7:4](https://ref.ly/Jude7:4) · [REV 11:2](https://ref.ly/Jude11:2) · [REV 13:5](https://ref.ly/Jude13:5) · [REV 14:1](https://ref.ly/Jude14:1) · [REV 14:3](https://ref.ly/Jude14:3) · [REV 21:17](https://ref.ly/Jude21:17)

67\.94 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** ἔτη τεσσεράκοντα

a very long time possibly a symbolic temporal expression denoting a very long period of time Though most translations render ἔτη τεσσεράκοντα as ‘forty years,’ the expression probably is to be understood as meaning an unusually long period of time. See also discussion at [67\.93](#67.93).

[ACT 7:30](https://ref.ly/John7:30) · [ACT 7:36](https://ref.ly/John7:36) · [ACT 7:42](https://ref.ly/John7:42) · [ACT 13:21](https://ref.ly/John13:21) · [HEB 3:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:10) · [HEB 3:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:17)

67\.93 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** ἡμέρας τεσσεράκοντα καὶ νύκτας τεσσεράκοντα

a long time (literally: forty days and forty nights) possibly a symbolic temporal expression denoting a relatively long period of time Most translations render ἡμέρας τεσσεράκοντα καὶ νύκτας τεσσεράκοντα as either ‘forty days and forty nights’ or ‘forty days,’ though it is possible, in view of the symbolic meaning of the number ‘forty,’ that this expression is to be understood as meaning a long period of time.

[MAT 4:2](https://ref.ly/Matt4:2) · [MAT 4:2](https://ref.ly/Matt4:2)

67\.93 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

**Collocation:** ἡμέρας τεσσεράκοντα

a long time (shortened form of \[c] literally, forty days) possibly a symbolic temporal expression denoting a relatively long period of time Most translations render ἡμέρας τεσσεράκοντα καὶ νύκτας τεσσεράκοντα as either ‘forty days and forty nights’ or ‘forty days,’ though it is possible, in view of the symbolic meaning of the number ‘forty,’ that this expression is to be understood as meaning a long period of time.

[MRK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Matt1:13) · [LUK 4:2](https://ref.ly/Mark4:2) · [ACT 1:3](https://ref.ly/John1:3)

* **Associated Passages:** John 2:20; Acts 4:22; Acts 7:30; Acts 7:42; Acts 23:13; Acts 23:21; 2 Corinthians 11:24; Revelation 7:4; Revelation 11:2; Revelation 13:5; Revelation 14:1; Revelation 14:3; Revelation 21:17; Acts 7:36; Acts 13:21; Hebrews 3:10; Hebrews 3:17; Matthew 4:2; Mark 1:13; Luke 4:2; Acts 1:3

## τετράπους (id: 004975000000000)

τετράπους
=========

τετράπους (G5074) — τετράπουν

adjc. \| \-ουν · gen. τετράποδος \| τέσσαρες \+ πούς

4\.4 · Animals · Animals

animal, quadruped any four\-footed animal, either wild or domesticated A high percentage of languages appear to have no generic term to identify all kinds of quadrupeds whether wild or domesticated. Rather, they tend to make quite clear distinctions between wild and domesticated animals, and therefore it may be necessary to indicate both types in those contexts where the reference is to both wild as well as domesticated animals. For example, one may sometimes speak of ‘animals of the grass and animals of the forest’ or ‘animals of the barn and animals of the mountains.’  
In [ACT 10:12](https://ref.ly/John10:12) the reference is primarily to wild animals, since for the most part wild animals would be those designated as unclean. However, swine were also regarded as unclean, and they were domesticated.

[ACT 10:12](https://ref.ly/John10:12) · [ACT 11:6](https://ref.ly/John11:6) · [ROM 1:23](https://ref.ly/Acts1:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 10:12; Acts 11:6; Romans 1:23

24\.36 · Sensory Events and States · See

## τηρέω (id: 004982000000000)

τηρέω
=====

τηρέω (G5083)

verb \| διατηρέω · παρατηρέω · παρατήρησις · συντηρέω

13\.32 · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · State

to cause to continue, to retain, to keep to cause a state to continue In [1CO 7:37](https://ref.ly/Rom7:37) the reference to ‘girl’ may be either a man’s daughter or a man’s fiancée. Because of the ambiguity of this statement in [1CO 7:37](https://ref.ly/Rom7:37) and in view of the cultural complications involved, especially because of differences of customs in different parts of the world, it is important that translators add a note at this point explaining the difference of interpretation and some of the cultural implications.

=======

noun, f. \| \-εως

37\.122 · Control, Rule · Guard, Watch Over

to guard, to keep watch, custody to continue to hold in custody The act of holding someone in custody or guarding an individual may be expressed as ‘standing guard to see that someone will not escape’ or ‘watching carefully so that one cannot run off’ or ‘tying someone up so that he cannot leave.’

7\.24 · Constructions · Buildings

jail, prison a place of detention Practically all languages have terms for a jail or a prison, though in some instances a descriptive phrase is employed, ‘a place where people are tied up’ or ‘a place to be chained.’ In some instances, highly idiomatic expressions are used, ‘a place for eating iron’ or ‘a room with rats.’

verb \| 3pl. τιθέασιν · ptc. τιθείς · impf.3sg. ἐτίθει · 3pl. ἐτίθουν, ἐτίθεσαν · fut. θήσω · aor. ἔθηκα · subj. θῶ · impv.2pl. θέτε · inf. θεῖναι · ptc. θείς · pf. τέθεικα · ptc. τεθεικώς · aor.midd.2sg. ἔθου · 3pl. ἔθεντο · impv.2pl. θέσθε · pf.pass.3sg. τέθειται · aor.pass. ἐτέθην · subj. τεθώ · inf. τεθῆναι \| ἄθεσμος · ἀθετέω · ἀθέτησις · ἀθῷος · ἀμετάθετος · ἀνάθεμα · ἀναθεματίζω · ἀνάθημα · ἀνατίθεμαι · ἀνεύθετος · ἀντιδιατίθημι · ἀντίθεσις · ἀποθήκη · ἀποτίθημι · ἀσύνθετος · διαθήκη · διατίθεμαι · ἔκθετος · ἐκτίθεμαι · ἐπίθεσις · ἐπιτίθημι · εὔθετος · θεμέλιον · θεμέλιος · θεμελιόω · θήκη · κατάθεμα · καταθεματίζω · κατατίθημι · μετάθεσις · μετατίθημι · νομοθεσία · νομοθετέομαι · νομοθέτης · νουθεσία · νουθετέω · ὁροθεσία · παραθήκη · παρατίθημι · περίθεσις · περιτίθημι · πρόθεσις · προθεσμία · προσανατίθεμαι · προστίθημι · προτίθεμαι · συγκατάθεσις · συγκατατίθεμαι · συνεπιτίθεμαι · συντίθεμαι · υἱοθεσία · ὑποτίθημι

to make up one’s mind, to decide (idioms, literally: to place in the heart, and: to place in the mind) to engage in the process of deciding It is also possible to interpret the phrase ἐν τῷ πνεύματι in [ACT 19:21](https://ref.ly/John19:21) as being a reference to the Holy Spirit and accordingly, the passage may be translated as ‘Paul, led by the Spirit, decided to travel through Macedonia.’

[ACT 4:35](https://ref.ly/John4:35) · [ACT 4:37](https://ref.ly/John4:37) · [ACT 5:2](https://ref.ly/John5:2)

17\.19 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Kneel

**Collocation:** τίθημι τὰ γόνατα

to kneel down, to kneel (an idiom, literally: to place the knees, a Latinism) to kneel down before, with the implication of an act of reverence or of supplication In a number of cultures, kneeling does not imply either reverence or an act of supplication. In some instances translators have used a functional substitute involving a similar type of stance, namely, ‘to bow low before,’ but it may be necessary to use a more or less literal description of ‘kneeling before’ and then to place in a marginal note an indication of the implications of such an act.

[MRK 15:19](https://ref.ly/Matt15:19) · [LUK 22:41](https://ref.ly/Mark22:41) · [ACT 7:60](https://ref.ly/John7:60) · [ACT 9:40](https://ref.ly/John9:40) · [ACT 20:36](https://ref.ly/John20:36) · [ACT 21:5](https://ref.ly/John21:5)

23\.113 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

**Collocation:** τὴν ψυχὴν τίθημι

to die voluntarily, to die willingly (an idiom, literally: to lay down one’s life) to die, with the implication of voluntary or willing action Though in English the phrases ‘to lay down one’s life’ or ‘to give one’s life’ do suggest a voluntary dying, a literal rendering of such expressions in other languages would not necessarily imply the same. It may therefore be necessary to use such expressions as ‘to die willingly’ or ‘to die without resisting.’ In some languages ‘willingly’ is expressed primarily as a negation of objecting, for example, ‘I will not object to dying.’

[JHN 10:11](https://ref.ly/Luke10:11) · [JHN 10:15](https://ref.ly/Luke10:15) · [JHN 10:17](https://ref.ly/Luke10:17) · [JHN 10:18](https://ref.ly/Luke10:18) · [JHN 10:18](https://ref.ly/Luke10:18) · [JHN 13:37](https://ref.ly/Luke13:37) · [JHN 13:38](https://ref.ly/Luke13:38) · [JHN 15:13](https://ref.ly/Luke15:13) · [1JN 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:16) · [1JN 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:16)

1 In this subdomain τίθημι\[a] is by far the most generic expression. 2 JHN 13:4 This seemingly unusual use of τίθημι with τὰ ἱμάτια in [JHN 13:4](https://ref.ly/Luke13:4) parallels the use of λαμβάνω in the sense of ‘putting on a garment’ in [JHN 13:12](https://ref.ly/Luke13:12) (see [49\.10](#49.10)). 3 Any meaning involving ‘to cause to be’ implies some change in state, and therefore one could classify these meanings under Subdomain B Change of State in Domain 13 Be, Become, Exist, Happen. However, the focus seems to be primarily upon the changed state rather than upon the process of moving from one state to another. The fact that a change of state has taken place seems to be semantically incidental.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:15; Matthew 12:18; Matthew 24:51; Matthew 27:60; Mark 4:21; Mark 6:29; Mark 6:56; Mark 10:16; Mark 12:36; Mark 15:46; Mark 15:47; Mark 16:6; Luke 5:18; Luke 6:48; Luke 8:16; Luke 11:33; Luke 12:46; Luke 14:29; Luke 20:43; Luke 23:53; Luke 23:55; John 2:10; John 11:34; John 19:19; John 19:41; John 19:42; John 20:2; John 20:13; John 20:15; Acts 3:2; Acts 4:3; Acts 5:15; Acts 5:18; Acts 5:25; Acts 7:16; Acts 9:37; Acts 12:4; Acts 13:29; Romans 9:33; Romans 14:13; 1 Corinthians 3:10; 1 Corinthians 3:11; 1 Corinthians 15:25; 1 Corinthians 16:2; 2 Corinthians 3:13; Hebrews 1:13; Hebrews 10:13; 1 Peter 2:6; Revelation 1:17; Revelation 10:2; Revelation 11:9; John 15:16; Acts 13:47; Acts 20:28; 1 Corinthians 12:28; 2 Corinthians 5:19; 1 Thessalonians 5:9; 1 Timothy 1:12; 1 Timothy 2:7; 2 Timothy 1:11; Hebrews 1:2; 1 Peter 2:8; John 13:4; Mark 4:30; 1 Corinthians 9:18; Luke 19:21; Luke 19:22; Matthew 22:44; Acts 1:7; Acts 2:35; Romans 4:17; 1 Corinthians 12:18; 2 Peter 2:6; Acts 27:12; Luke 9:44; Luke 1:66; Luke 21:14; Acts 5:4; Acts 19:21; Acts 4:35; Acts 4:37; Acts 5:2; Mark 15:19; Luke 22:41; Acts 7:60; Acts 9:40; Acts 20:36; Acts 21:5; John 10:11; John 10:15; John 10:17; John 10:18; John 13:37; John 13:38; John 15:13; 1 John 3:16


## τίκτω (id: 004987000000000)

τίκτω
=====

τίκτω (G5088)

verb \| fut. τέξομαι · aor. ἔτεκον · inf. τεκεῖν · aor.pass. ἐτέχθην · ptc. τεχθείς \| ἀρχιτέκτων · ἄτεκνος · ὁμότεχνος · πρωτοτόκια · πρωτότοκος · τεκνίον · τεκνογονέω · τεκνογονία · τέκνον · τεκνοτροφέω · τέκτων · τόκος · φιλότεκνος

23\.52 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

to bear, to give birth to give birth to a child1 All languages have expressions for human birth, though these are frequently in idiomatic forms, for example, ‘to drop a child’ or ‘to cause a baby to pass between the legs.’ A number of languages have a variety of terms referring to giving birth, and some of these may involve unfortunate connotations. One must therefore be careful about the selection of appropriate expressions.

[MAT 1:21](https://ref.ly/Matt1:21) · [MAT 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) · [MAT 1:25](https://ref.ly/Matt1:25) · [MAT 2:2](https://ref.ly/Matt2:2) · [LUK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Mark1:31) · [LUK 1:57](https://ref.ly/Mark1:57) · [LUK 2:6](https://ref.ly/Mark2:6) · [LUK 2:7](https://ref.ly/Mark2:7) · [LUK 2:11](https://ref.ly/Mark2:11) · [JHN 16:21](https://ref.ly/Luke16:21) · [GAL 4:27](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:27) · [JAS 1:15](https://ref.ly/Heb1:15) · [REV 12:2](https://ref.ly/Jude12:2) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4) · [REV 12:5](https://ref.ly/Jude12:5) · [REV 12:13](https://ref.ly/Jude12:13)

to grow, to produce to cause the growth and production of plants

[HEB 6:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:7)

1 It is possible that τεκνογονέω and τεκνογονία differ somewhat in connotation from τίκτω\[a] and γεννάω\[b] in being stylistically more formal, but there seems to be no significant denotative distinction in meaning.

## τιμή (id: 004991000000000)

τιμή
====

τιμή (G5092)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| τιμάω

87\.4 · Status · Honor or Respect in Relation to Status

honor, respect, status honor as an element in the assignment of status to a person

[JHN 4:44](https://ref.ly/Luke4:44) · [ROM 2:7](https://ref.ly/Acts2:7) · [ROM 2:10](https://ref.ly/Acts2:10) · [ROM 12:10](https://ref.ly/Acts12:10) · [ROM 13:7](https://ref.ly/Acts13:7) · [ROM 13:7](https://ref.ly/Acts13:7) · [1CO 12:23](https://ref.ly/Rom12:23) · [1CO 12:24](https://ref.ly/Rom12:24) · [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) · [1TI 1:17](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:17) · [1TI 6:1](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:1) · [1TI 6:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:16) · [HEB 2:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:7) · [HEB 2:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:9) · [HEB 3:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm3:3) · [HEB 5:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:4) · [1PE 1:7](https://ref.ly/Jas1:7) · [1PE 3:7](https://ref.ly/Jas3:7) · [2PE 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:17) · [REV 4:9](https://ref.ly/Jude4:9) · [REV 4:11](https://ref.ly/Jude4:11) · [REV 5:12](https://ref.ly/Jude5:12) · [REV 5:13](https://ref.ly/Jude5:13) · [REV 7:12](https://ref.ly/Jude7:12)

65\.1 · Value · Valuable, Lacking in Value

worth, value the worth or merit of some object, event, or state In some languages the equivalent of ‘value’ is almost always in terms of ‘importance.’ This is particularly true if one is speaking of objects which are normally not bought and sold. Accordingly, one may render this particular expression in [1CO 12:23](https://ref.ly/Rom12:23) as ‘those parts of the body which we think of as not being so important, to these we grant particular importance’ or ‘... we consider as being very important.’  
It is also possible to interpret τιμή in [1CO 12:23](https://ref.ly/Rom12:23) as a degree of honor or appreciation (see τιμή\[a], [87\.4](#87.4)).

[ROM 9:21](https://ref.ly/Acts9:21) · [1CO 12:23](https://ref.ly/Rom12:23) · [COL 2:23](https://ref.ly/Phil2:23) · [2TI 2:20](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:20) · [2TI 2:21](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:21) · [1PE 2:7](https://ref.ly/Jas2:7) · [2PE 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:17) · [REV 21:26](https://ref.ly/Jude21:26)

57\.161 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Pay, Price, Cost

amount, price, cost the amount of money or property regarded as representing the value or price of something It would be wrong to assume that τιμή in [1CO 7:23](https://ref.ly/Rom7:23) necessarily means ‘a high price.’ The notion ‘high’ comes from the contextual reference to the death of Christ. In [1CO 7:23](https://ref.ly/Rom7:23), however, the implication is that a price was set and that the payment has been made. If the passive expression in [1CO 7:23](https://ref.ly/Rom7:23) must be made active, one may translate as ‘Christ bought you with a price’ or ‘Christ paid for you.’

[MAT 27:6](https://ref.ly/Matt27:6) · [MAT 27:9](https://ref.ly/Matt27:9) · [ACT 4:34](https://ref.ly/John4:34) · [ACT 5:2](https://ref.ly/John5:2) · [ACT 5:3](https://ref.ly/John5:3) · [ACT 7:16](https://ref.ly/John7:16) · [ACT 19:19](https://ref.ly/John19:19) · [1CO 6:20](https://ref.ly/Rom6:20) · [1CO 7:23](https://ref.ly/Rom7:23)

57\.167 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Pay, Price, Cost

compensation, pay, honorarium compensation given for special service, with the implication that this is a way by which honor or respect may be shown τιμή\[d] in the sense of compensation is related in meaning to τιμάω\[c] to support, to provide for ([57\.117](#57.117)) and τιμή\[c] cost ([57\.161](#57.161)), but in [1TI 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:17) it is also possible to understand τιμή in the sense of τιμή\[a] honor, respect ([87\.4](#87.4)), and therefore one may speak of the elders as receiving double honor.

[ACT 28:10](https://ref.ly/John28:10) · [1TI 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:17)

* **Associated Passages:** John 4:44; Romans 2:7; Romans 2:10; Romans 12:10; Romans 13:7; 1 Corinthians 12:23; 1 Corinthians 12:24; 1 Thessalonians 4:4; 1 Timothy 1:17; 1 Timothy 6:1; 1 Timothy 6:16; Hebrews 2:7; Hebrews 2:9; Hebrews 3:3; Hebrews 5:4; 1 Peter 1:7; 1 Peter 3:7; 2 Peter 1:17; Revelation 4:9; Revelation 4:11; Revelation 5:12; Revelation 5:13; Revelation 7:12; Romans 9:21; Colossians 2:23; 2 Timothy 2:20; 2 Timothy 2:21; 1 Peter 2:7; Revelation 21:26; Matthew 27:6; Matthew 27:9; Acts 4:34; Acts 5:2; Acts 5:3; Acts 7:16; Acts 19:19; 1 Corinthians 6:20; 1 Corinthians 7:23; Acts 28:10; 1 Timothy 5:17


## τίμιος (id: 004992000000000)

τίμιος
======

τίμιος (G5093)

adjc. \| \-α, \-ον \| τιμάω

65\.2 · Value · Valuable, Lacking in Value

valuable, precious pertaining to being of considerable value or worth It is possible to interpret λίθους τιμίους in [1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12) as a unit which means ‘precious stones’ (see [2\.29](#2.29)), but in this figurative context of a foundation, the reference may very well be more general.

[ACT 20:24](https://ref.ly/John20:24) · [1CO 3:12](https://ref.ly/Rom3:12) · [JAS 5:7](https://ref.ly/Heb5:7) · [1PE 1:19](https://ref.ly/Jas1:19) · [2PE 1:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:4) · [REV 17:4](https://ref.ly/Jude17:4) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) · [REV 18:16](https://ref.ly/Jude18:16) · [REV 21:11](https://ref.ly/Jude21:11) · [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19)

87\.6 · Status · Honor or Respect in Relation to Status

honored, respected pertaining to high status, involving both honor and respect

[ACT 5:34](https://ref.ly/John5:34) · [HEB 13:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 20:24; 1 Corinthians 3:12; James 5:7; 1 Peter 1:19; 2 Peter 1:4; Revelation 17:4; Revelation 18:12; Revelation 18:16; Revelation 21:11; Revelation 21:19; Acts 5:34; Hebrews 13:4


## τιμιότης (id: 004993000000000)

τιμιότης
========

τιμιότης (G5094)

noun, f. \| \-ητος \| τιμάω

57\.35 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Be Rich, Be Wealthy

wealth, riches (derivative of τίμιος\[a] ‘valuable, precious,’ [65\.2](#65.2)) a large quantity of costly, valuable possessions ‘Wealth’ may usually be rendered by ‘the many valuable possessions.’

[REV 18:19](https://ref.ly/Jude18:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 18:19

92\.15 · Discourse Referentials · Whom or What Spoken or Written About

why? for what reason? an interrogative reference to reason The expression τί ἐμοὶ καὶ σοί (literally ‘what for me and you?’) in [JHN 2:4](https://ref.ly/Luke2:4) is an adage meaning ‘for what reason are you saying or doing this to me?’ In some languages it may be preferable to translate [JHN 2:4](https://ref.ly/Luke2:4) as ‘why do you ask me this?’ In [MRK 1:24](https://ref.ly/Matt1:24) one may translate ‘what do you want with us?’

## τὶς (id: 005000000000000)

92\.13 · Discourse Referentials · Whom or What Spoken or Written About

someone important, something important (occurring only in a predicate position) a reference to someone or something of prominence or distinction For a treatment of τις\[b] as part of an idiom in [ACT 5:36](https://ref.ly/John5:36), see [87\.49](#87.49).

## Τίτιος (id: 005001000000000)

Τίτιος
======

Τίτιος (G5103a)

noun\-name, m. \| \-ου

93\.363 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

τοιγαροῦν
=========

τοιγαροῦν (G5105)

conj. \| τοί \+ γάρ \+ οῦν

89\.51 · Relations · Result

for this very reason, therefore, hence, therefore indeed, so then an emphatic marker of result, often associated with exhortation

[1TH 4:8](https://ref.ly/Col4:8) · [HEB 12:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:1)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Thessalonians 4:8; Hebrews 12:1

## τοῖχος (id: 005008000000000)

τοῖχος
======

τοῖχος (G5109)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| μεσότοιχον · τεῖχος

7\.46 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

wall wall of a house or enclosure A literal translation of the phrase ‘whitewashed wall’ is rarely meaningful. Sometimes one can use a descriptive phrase such as ‘a dirty wall which is made to look white’ or ‘... to look clean.’ In other instances one may wish to focus upon the function suggested by the idiom ‘whitewashed wall’ and employ a phrase such as ‘one who has been made to look good but really isn’t.’

[ACT 23:3](https://ref.ly/John23:3)

88\.234 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Hypocrisy, Pretense

**Collocation:** τοῖχος κεκονιαμένος

hypocrite, impostor (an idiom, literally: whitewashed wall) one who pretends to be one thing, while in reality he is something quite different

[ACT 23:3](https://ref.ly/John23:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 23:3

noun, m. \| \-ου \| ἄτοπος · ἐντόπιος

80\.1 · Space · Space, Place

space, place, room an area of any size, regarded in certain contexts as a point in space In [JHN 11:48](https://ref.ly/Luke11:48) the expression τὸν τόπον refers to the Temple in Jerusalem.

[MAT 12:43](https://ref.ly/Matt12:43) · [MAT 14:13](https://ref.ly/Matt14:13) · [MAT 14:15](https://ref.ly/Matt14:15) · [MAT 14:35](https://ref.ly/Matt14:35) · [MAT 24:7](https://ref.ly/Matt24:7) ·
