2:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:14) · [1TH 1:8](https://ref.ly/Col1:8) · [1TI 2:8](https://ref.ly/2Thess2:8) · [HEB 8:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:7) · [HEB 11:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:8) · [HEB 12:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:17) · [2PE 1:19](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:19) · [REV 2:5](https://ref.ly/Jude2:5) · [REV 6:14](https://ref.ly/Jude6:14) · [REV 12:6](https://ref.ly/Jude12:6) · [REV 12:8](https://ref.ly/Jude12:8) · [REV 12:14](https://ref.ly/Jude12:14) · [REV 16:16](https://ref.ly/Jude16:16) · [REV 20:11](https://ref.ly/Jude20:11)

33\.10 · Communication · Word, Passage

passage, part of a document, part of Scripture a particular portion or unit of discourse In rendering τόπος\[b], περιοχή, or γραφή\[a], it is often possible to use a rather general term such as the place or the part. In other instances one may wish to use a term meaning the words. Accordingly, [LUK 4:21](https://ref.ly/Mark4:21) may be rendered as ‘these words have come true today as you have heard them being read.’

[LUK 4:17](https://ref.ly/Mark4:17)

42\.21 · Perform, Do · Do, Perform

position of service, task a role involving activity and responsibility In some languages the latter part of this expression in [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) may be rendered as ‘helping in this way and being an apostle’ or ‘helping in this way as an apostle.’ For another interpretation of τόπος in [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25), see [87\.1](#87.1).

[ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) · [REV 18:17](https://ref.ly/Jude18:17)

87\.1 · Status · Position, Rank

position, role the position of a person within a group, implying a particular role or type of activity In a number of languages the equivalent of this expression in [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) may be simply ‘to undertake the work of an apostle’ or ‘to be an apostle in serving.’ For another interpretation of τόπος in [ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25), involving a shift in focus, see [42\.21](#42.21).

[ACT 1:25](https://ref.ly/John1:25) · [1CO 14:16](https://ref.ly/Rom14:16)

71\.6 · Mode · Possible, Impossible

possibility, chance, opportunity the possibility of some occasion or opportunity

[ACT 25:16](https://ref.ly/John25:16) · [ROM 12:19](https://ref.ly/Acts12:19) · [ROM 15:23](https://ref.ly/Acts15:23) · [EPH 4:27](https://ref.ly/Gal4:27) · [HEB 12:17](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:17)

11\.59 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

place, people the inhabitants of a place1 In a number of languages it is impossible to use a term meaning ‘place’ as a reference to the people of such a place.

[MRK 6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11)

1\.68 · Geographical Objects and Features · Land in Contrast With the Sea

**Collocation:** τόπος διθάλασσος

sandbar, reef a bar or reef produced in an area where two currents meet It is possible to understand τόπος διθάλασσος in [ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41) as a place of crosscurrents; see [14\.32](#14.32). In some languages it may be necessary to construct a descriptive equivalent for ‘sandbank,’ for example, ‘a hill of sand just beneath the surface of the water’ or ‘a ridge of sand hidden by the water.’

[ACT 27:41](https://ref.ly/John27:41)

1 It is possible that in the case of such meanings as τόπος\[f] ([11\.59](#11.59)), πόλις\[c] ([11\.61](#11.61)), κώμη\[b] ([11\.62](#11.62)), and χώρα\[e] ([11\.64](#11.64)) one should count on certain more or less automatic semantic rules by which the meaning of inhabitants could be derived by metonymy from expressions of place. Since, however, such metonymic developments are far from universal, the distinct meanings are listed here as a practical guide to translators. The same type of problem occurs with Ιεροσόλυμα ‘Jerusalem,’ Ἰουδαία ‘Judea,’ and περίχωρος ‘region’ in [MAT 3:5](https://ref.ly/Matt3:5).

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:43; Matthew 14:13; Matthew 14:15; Matthew 14:35; Matthew 24:7; Matthew 24:15; Matthew 26:52; Matthew 27:33; Matthew 28:6; Mark 1:35; Mark 1:45; Mark 6:31; Mark 6:32; Mark 6:35; Mark 13:8; Mark 15:22; Mark 16:6; Luke 2:7; Luke 4:37; Luke 4:42; Luke 6:17; Luke 9:12; Luke 10:1; Luke 10:32; Luke 11:1; Luke 11:24; Luke 14:9; Luke 14:10; Luke 14:22; Luke 16:28; Luke 19:5; Luke 21:11; Luke 22:40; Luke 23:33; John 4:20; John 5:13; John 6:10; John 6:23; John 10:40; John 11:6; John 11:30; John 11:48; John 14:2; John 14:3; John 18:2; John 19:13; John 19:17; John 19:20; John 19:41; John 20:7; Acts 1:25; Acts 4:31; Acts 6:13; Acts 6:14; Acts 7:7; Acts 7:33; Acts 7:49; Acts 12:17; Acts 16:3; Acts 21:28; Acts 27:2; Acts 27:8; Acts 27:29; Acts 28:7; Romans 9:26; 1 Corinthians 1:2; 2 Corinthians 2:14; 1 Thessalonians 1:8; 1 Timothy 2:8; Hebrews 8:7; Hebrews 11:8; Hebrews 12:17; 2 Peter 1:19; Revelation 2:5; Revelation 6:14; Revelation 12:6; Revelation 12:8; Revelation 12:14; Revelation 16:16; Revelation 20:11; Luke 4:17; Revelation 18:17; 1 Corinthians 14:16; Acts 25:16; Romans 12:19; Romans 15:23; Ephesians 4:27; Mark 6:11; Acts 27:41


## τοσοῦτος (id: 005017000000000)

τοσοῦτος
========

τοσοῦτος (G5118)

pdem. \| \-η, \-ον \| οὗτος

59\.6 · Quantity · Many, Few \[Countables]

so many, this many pertaining to a quantity of objects or events considerably beyond normal expectations

[MAT 15:33](https://ref.ly/Matt15:33) · [LUK 15:29](https://ref.ly/Mark15:29) · [JHN 6:9](https://ref.ly/Luke6:9) · [JHN 12:37](https://ref.ly/Luke12:37) · [JHN 21:11](https://ref.ly/Luke21:11) · [1CO 14:10](https://ref.ly/Rom14:10) · [GAL 3:4](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:4)

59\.18 · Quantity · Much, Little \[Masses, Collectives, Extensions]

so much, so great, such a large pertaining to a quantity considerably beyond normal expectations

[MAT 8:10](https://ref.ly/Matt8:10) · [MAT 15:33](https://ref.ly/Matt15:33) · [LUK 7:9](https://ref.ly/Mark7:9) · [JHN 14:9](https://ref.ly/Luke14:9) · [ACT 5:8](https://ref.ly/John5:8) · [ACT 5:8](https://ref.ly/John5:8) · [HEB 4:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:7) · [HEB 12:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:1) · [REV 18:17](https://ref.ly/Jude18:17)

78\.52 · Degree · Up To, As Much As, To the Degree That \[Marked Extent of Degree]

to the degree that, to the same degree, as much as a degree of correlative extent It is also possible to render this portion of [REV 18:7](https://ref.ly/Jude18:7) as ‘to the degree that she glorified herself and lived in luxury, to that same degree give her torment and sorrow.’  
Expressions involving correspondence of degrees must often be rather considerably restructured. For example, in the first part of [REV 18:7](https://ref.ly/Jude18:7) one may translate in some languages ‘she honored herself very much and lived in great luxury, and so give her very much suffering and grief.’ In the case of [HEB 1:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:4), one may translate ‘God gave his Son a name that was more important than the name of the angels; therefore, God’s Son is greater than the angels.’

[HEB 1:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:4) · [HEB 7:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:22) · [HEB 10:25](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:25) · [REV 18:7](https://ref.ly/Jude18:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 15:33; Luke 15:29; John 6:9; John 12:37; John 21:11; 1 Corinthians 14:10; Galatians 3:4; Matthew 8:10; Luke 7:9; John 14:9; Acts 5:8; Hebrews 4:7; Hebrews 12:1; Revelation 18:17; Hebrews 1:4; Hebrews 7:22; Hebrews 10:25; Revelation 18:7


## τότε (id: 005018000000000)

τότε
====

τότε (G5119)

advb. \| ὅς \+ τέ

67\.47 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Other Points of Time: Before, Long Ago, Now, At the Same Time, When, About, After

then a point of time subsequent to another point of time

## τράγος (id: 005019000000000)

τράγος
======

τράγος (G5131)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| τρώγω

4\.21 · Animals · Animals

he\-goat male goat (smaller domesticated four\-footed animal with hooves; genus Capra; source of meat, hides, hair, and horns) A number of languages have special terms for ‘he\-goat’ and ‘she\-goat,’ and frequently there is no formal relationship between the respective terms any more than there is in English between billy and nanny or between the corresponding terms for sheep, namely, ram and ewe.

[HEB 9:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:12) · [HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13) · [HEB 10:4](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 9:12; Hebrews 9:13; Hebrews 10:4


## τράπεζα (id: 005020000000000)

τράπεζα
=======

τράπεζα (G5132)

noun, f. \| \-ης \| τέσσαρες \+ πεζεύω

6\.113 · Artifacts · Furniture

table a generic expression for any type of table

[MAT 15:27](https://ref.ly/Matt15:27) · [MAT 21:12](https://ref.ly/Matt21:12) · [MRK 7:28](https://ref.ly/Matt7:28) · [MRK 11:15](https://ref.ly/Matt11:15) · [LUK 16:21](https://ref.ly/Mark16:21) · [LUK 22:21](https://ref.ly/Mark22:21) · [LUK 22:30](https://ref.ly/Mark22:30) · [JHN 2:15](https://ref.ly/Luke2:15) · [ROM 11:9](https://ref.ly/Acts11:9) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [HEB 9:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:2)

23\.26 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

a meal (a figurative extension of meaning of τράπεζα\[a] ‘table,’ [6\.113](#6.113)) a meal, with possible emphasis upon its being relatively bountiful

[ACT 16:34](https://ref.ly/John16:34) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21)

57\.215 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Lend, Loan, Interest, Borrow, Bank

bank a place where money is kept or managed or where credit is established

[LUK 19:23](https://ref.ly/Mark19:23)

34\.32 · Association · Belong To, Be Included in the Membership of, Be Excluded From

**Collocation:** τραπέζης μετέχω

to belong to (a religious group), to eat at the table of (an idiom, literally: to share in a table) to belong to a particular religious group as evidenced by ceremonial eating1

[1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21) · [1CO 10:21](https://ref.ly/Rom10:21)

57\.230 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Keep Records

**Collocation:** διακονέω τραπέζαις

to handle finances (an idiom, literally: to serve tables) to be responsible for financial aspects of an enterprise It is also possible to interpret the phrase διακονέω τραπέζαις not as an idiom but simply as ‘to wait on tables, to serve meals’ (see [23\.26](#23.26) and [46\.13](#46.13)), but even so the context relates to caring for needs.

[ACT 6:2](https://ref.ly/John6:2)

1 It is not possible to determine on the basis of existing evidence whether the expression τραπέζης μετέχω is a genuine idiom or a phrase which is to be taken in a literal sense as referring to the ordinance of Holy Communion in contrast to banqueting in heathen temples.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 15:27; Matthew 21:12; Mark 7:28; Mark 11:15; Luke 16:21; Luke 22:21; Luke 22:30; John 2:15; Romans 11:9; 1 Corinthians 10:21; Hebrews 9:2; Acts 16:34; Luke 19:23; Acts 6:2

## τραχηλίζω (id: 005024000000000)

## τράχηλος (id: 005025000000000)

τράχηλος
========

τράχηλος (G5137)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| τραχηλίζομαι

8\.25 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

neck τράχηλος also occurs in the NT in certain idiomatic expressions, for example, ‘to fall on the neck of someone’ ([LUK 15:20](https://ref.ly/Mark15:20) and [ACT 20:37](https://ref.ly/John20:37)) in the sense of ‘to embrace’ ([34\.64](#34.64)), and ‘to put down their necks’ ([ROM 16:4](https://ref.ly/Acts16:4)) meaning ‘to risk their lives’ ([21\.8](#21.8)). It is rare indeed that one can translate such idioms literally, since ‘to fall on the neck of someone’ may readily suggest a murderous attack, and ‘to risk one’s neck’ may be simply meaningless, since the custom of beheading as a means of execution may be relatively unknown.

[MAT 18:6](https://ref.ly/Matt18:6) · [MRK 9:42](https://ref.ly/Matt9:42) · [LUK 15:20](https://ref.ly/Mark15:20) · [LUK 17:2](https://ref.ly/Mark17:2) · [ACT 15:10](https://ref.ly/John15:10) · [ACT 20:37](https://ref.ly/John20:37)

21\.8 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Expose Oneself to Danger

**Collocation:** τράχηλον ὑποτίθημι

to risk one’s life (an idiom, literally: to put down the neck) willingly and purposely to expose oneself to extreme danger and risk In some instances one can translate this expression in [ROM 16:4](https://ref.ly/Acts16:4) as ‘who showed they were willing to die in order that I could live’ or ‘in order to help me continue to live, they almost died.’

[ROM 16:4](https://ref.ly/Acts16:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 18:6; Mark 9:42; Luke 15:20; Luke 17:2; Acts 15:10; Acts 20:37; Romans 16:4

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:40; Matthew 13:33; Matthew 15:32; Matthew 17:4; Matthew 18:16; Matthew 18:20; Matthew 26:61; Matthew 27:40; Matthew 27:63; Mark 8:2; Mark 8:31; Mark 9:5; Mark 9:31; Mark 10:34; Mark 14:58; Mark 15:29; Luke 1:56; Luke 2:46; Luke 4:25; Luke 9:33; Luke 10:36; Luke 11:5; Luke 12:52; Luke 13:7; Luke 13:21; John 2:6; John 2:19; John 2:20; John 21:11; Acts 5:7; Acts 7:20; Acts 9:9; Acts 11:11; Acts 17:2; Acts 19:8; Acts 20:3; Acts 25:1; Acts 28:7; Acts 28:11; Acts 28:12; Acts 28:15; Acts 28:17; 1 Corinthians 10:8; 1 Corinthians 13:13; 1 Corinthians 14:27; 1 Corinthians 14:29; 2 Corinthians 13:1; Galatians 1:18; 1 Timothy 5:19; Hebrews 10:28; James 5:17; 1 John 5:7; 1 John 5:8; Revelation 6:6; Revelation 8:13; Revelation 9:18; Revelation 11:9; Revelation 11:11; Revelation 16:13; Revelation 16:19; Revelation 21:13


## τρέμω (id: 005029000000000)

τρέμω
=====

τρέμω (G5141)

verb \| ἔντρομος · τρόμος

16\.6 · Non\-Linear Movement

to tremble, trembling, to quiver, to shake to shake or tremble, often with the implication of fear and/or consternation In a number of languages there are two distinct terms for trembling, one relating to illness (as in the case of epileptic seizures or the chills and fever associated with malaria) and the other associated with fear.

[MRK 5:33](https://ref.ly/Matt5:33) · [LUK 8:47](https://ref.ly/Mark8:47)

25\.259 · Attitudes and Emotions · Fear, Terror, Alarm

to fear, to have awesome respect for (a figurative extension of meaning of τρέμω\[a] ‘to tremble,’ [16\.6](#16.6)) to be so afraid as to tremble, often with the implication of awe1 For another interpretation of τρέμω in [2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10), see [87\.14](#87.14).

[2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10)

87\.14 · Status · Honor or Respect in Relation to Status

to fear, to show great reverence for, to show great respect for to have such awe or respect for a person as to involve a measure of fear In a number of languages there are serious problems involved in speaking of ‘fearing God,’ for this might imply merely ‘to be scared of God’ as though God were some kind of bogeyman. If there is a term with the meaning of ‘awe’ (perhaps in a phrase such as ‘to stand in awe of’), this may be an adequate equivalent. In some instances awe is expressed idiomatically as ‘to stand with one’s heart in one’s throat’ or ‘to be in someone’s presence with one’s heart beating fast.’  
For another interpretation of τρέμω in [2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10), see [25\.259](#25.259).

[2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10)

1 It is possible to regard τρέμω\[b] ([25\.259](#25.259)) and φρίσσω ([25\.260](#25.260)) as belonging simultaneously to two quite distinct semantic domains, the one being physiological, that is to say, a type of uncontrolled physical response because of fear or great awe, and a psychological experience of fear or terror. Since, however, it is the latter which gives rise to the former, one would seem to be more justified in treating these meanings as matters of emotive responses rather than as physiological events.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 5:33; Luke 8:47; 2 Peter 2:10

verb \| aor. ἔθρεψα · pf.pass. τέθραμμαι \| ἀνατρέφω · διατροφή · ἐκτρέφω · ἐντρέφομαι · θρέμμα · θρόμβος · σύντροφος · τεκνοτροφέω · τροφή · τροφός · τροφοφορέω

to raise, to rear, to bring up to raise a child to maturity by providing for physical and psychological needs2 To raise or bring up children may be expressed in a number of different ways, for example, ‘to give food to children,’ ‘to take care of children,’ ‘to be a parent to children,’ ‘to cause a child to become an adult,’ or ‘to make a child become like oneself.’

[LUK 4:16](https://ref.ly/Mark4:16)

1 It is possible that ἐκτρέφω\[a] is somewhat more emphatic in meaning than τρέφω\[a], but this cannot be determined from existing contexts. 2 There may very well be subtle differences of meaning in the series in [35\.51](#35.51), but there is no direct contextual evidence to support significant distinctions in meaning.

noun, n. \| \-τος

6\.216 · Artifacts · Miscellaneous

hole a small opening1 (used in the NT only with reference to the so\-called ‘eye’ of a needle) The hole in a needle is variously referred to in different languages, for example, ‘the nostril of the needle,’ ‘the ear of the needle,’ ‘the mouth of the needle,’ and even ‘the anus of the needle.’

## τρίτος (id: 005043000000000)

τρίτος
======

τρίτος (G5154)

adjc. \| \-η, \-ον \| τρεῖς

60\.50 · Number · First, Second, Third, Etc. \[Ordinals]

third third in a series involving either time, space, or set1

[MAT 16:21](https://ref.ly/Matt16:21) · [MAT 17:23](https://ref.ly/Matt17:23) · [MAT 20:3](https://ref.ly/Matt20:3) · [MAT 20:19](https://ref.ly/Matt20:19) · [MAT 22:26](https://ref.ly/Matt22:26) · [MAT 26:44](https://ref.ly/Matt26:44) · [MAT 27:64](https://ref.ly/Matt27:64) · [MRK 12:21](https://ref.ly/Matt12:21) · [MRK 14:41](https://ref.ly/Matt14:41) · [MRK 15:25](https://ref.ly/Matt15:25) · [LUK 9:22](https://ref.ly/Mark9:22) · [LUK 12:38](https://ref.ly/Mark12:38) · [LUK 13:32](https://ref.ly/Mark13:32) · [LUK 18:33](https://ref.ly/Mark18:33) · [LUK 20:12](https://ref.ly/Mark20:12) · [LUK 20:31](https://ref.ly/Mark20:31) · [LUK 23:22](https://ref.ly/Mark23:22) · [LUK 24:7](https://ref.ly/Mark24:7) · [LUK 24:21](https://ref.ly/Mark24:21) · [LUK 24:46](https://ref.ly/Mark24:46) · [JHN 2:1](https://ref.ly/Luke2:1) · [JHN 21:14](https://ref.ly/Luke21:14) · [JHN 21:17](https://ref.ly/Luke21:17) · [JHN 21:17](https://ref.ly/Luke21:17) · [ACT 2:15](https://ref.ly/John2:15) · [ACT 10:40](https://ref.ly/John10:40) · [ACT 23:23](https://ref.ly/John23:23) · [ACT 27:19](https://ref.ly/John27:19) · [1CO 12:28](https://ref.ly/Rom12:28) · [1CO 15:4](https://ref.ly/Rom15:4) · [2CO 12:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:2) · [2CO 12:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:14) · [2CO 13:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor13:1) · [REV 4:7](https://ref.ly/Jude4:7) · [REV 6:5](https://ref.ly/Jude6:5) · [REV 6:5](https://ref.ly/Jude6:5) · [REV 8:10](https://ref.ly/Jude8:10) · [REV 11:14](https://ref.ly/Jude11:14) · [REV 14:9](https://ref.ly/Jude14:9) · [REV 16:4](https://ref.ly/Jude16:4) · [REV 21:19](https://ref.ly/Jude21:19)

60\.63 · Number · Half, Third, Fourth \[Fractional Part]

third, third part a third part of an object, series, or mass In a number of languages a fractional part of something is referred to by means of ordinal numbers. For example, ‘a third of the trees’ would be rendered as ‘every third tree,’ and ‘a third of the earth was consumed by fire’ would be rendered as ‘the third part of the earth was consumed by fire’ or ‘having divided the earth into three parts, one part was destroyed by fire.’

[REV 8:7](https://ref.ly/Jude8:7) · [REV 8:7](https://ref.ly/Jude8:7) · [REV 8:8](https://ref.ly/Jude8:8) · [REV 8:9](https://ref.ly/Jude8:9) · [REV 8:9](https://ref.ly/Jude8:9) · [REV 8:10](https://ref.ly/Jude8:10) · [REV 8:11](https://ref.ly/Jude8:11) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 9:15](https://ref.ly/Jude9:15) · [REV 9:18](https://ref.ly/Jude9:18) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4)

1 Though τὸ τρίτον functions in an adverbial sense, there seems to be no reason to set up a separate meaning of τρίτος as referring only to a temporal sequence. The interpretation of τρίτος in terms of time or space is a factor of the context. When objects are involved, ordinals simply mark position in a spacial sequence; when events are involved, ordinals simply mark position in a temporal sequence.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 16:21; Matthew 17:23; Matthew 20:3; Matthew 20:19; Matthew 22:26; Matthew 26:44; Matthew 27:64; Mark 12:21; Mark 14:41; Mark 15:25; Luke 9:22; Luke 12:38; Luke 13:32; Luke 18:33; Luke 20:12; Luke 20:31; Luke 23:22; Luke 24:7; Luke 24:21; Luke 24:46; John 2:1; John 21:14; John 21:17; Acts 2:15; Acts 10:40; Acts 23:23; Acts 27:19; 1 Corinthians 12:28; 1 Corinthians 15:4; 2 Corinthians 12:2; 2 Corinthians 12:14; 2 Corinthians 13:1; Revelation 4:7; Revelation 6:5; Revelation 8:10; Revelation 11:14; Revelation 14:9; Revelation 16:4; Revelation 21:19; Revelation 8:7; Revelation 8:8; Revelation 8:9; Revelation 8:11; Revelation 8:12; Revelation 9:15; Revelation 9:18; Revelation 12:4

## τροφή (id: 005049000000000)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| τρέφω

5\.1 · Foods and Condiments · Food

food any kind of food or nourishment1 Almost all languages have at least a few general terms for food, though these may be derived from verbal expressions meaning essentially ‘that which is eaten.’ In some instances a distinction may be made between ‘that which is chewed’ and ‘that which is drunk,’ and it may therefore be important in certain contexts to speak of food in general by a phrase meaning ‘that which is either chewed or drunk.’ If one fails to include both types of food, the reader might interpret a passage such as [MAT 6:11](https://ref.ly/Matt6:11) as requesting only solid foods.  
In the place of a general term or phrase such as ‘that which is eaten’ or ‘that which is consumed,’ some languages generalize the meaning of a particular term. For example, in certain parts of the Orient the term meaning specifically ‘rice’ also refers to ‘food’ in general. In fact, some persons will declare, ‘I have not eaten!’ if they have not had rice as part of a meal. A similar type of meaning has developed in English with respect to ‘bread.’ For example, in rendering [LUK 4:4](https://ref.ly/Mark4:4) (οὐκ ἐπ’ ἄρτῳ μόνῳ ζήσεται ὁ ἄνθρωπος ‘man shall not live by bread alone’) it would be wrong to employ a strictly literal rendering, since this might mean simply that people should not live on a diet consisting solely of bread. The meaning of [LUK 4:4](https://ref.ly/Mark4:4) is, of course, ‘to live means more than merely eating.’

[MAT 3:4](https://ref.ly/Matt3:4) · [MAT 6:25](https://ref.ly/Matt6:25) · [MAT 10:10](https://ref.ly/Matt10:10)2 · [MAT 24:45](https://ref.ly/Matt24:45) · [LUK 12:23](https://ref.ly/Mark12:23) · [JHN 4:8](https://ref.ly/Luke4:8) · [ACT 2:46](https://ref.ly/John2:46) · [ACT 9:19](https://ref.ly/John9:19) · [ACT 14:17](https://ref.ly/John14:17) · [ACT 27:33](https://ref.ly/John27:33) · [ACT 27:34](https://ref.ly/John27:34) · [ACT 27:36](https://ref.ly/John27:36) · [ACT 27:38](https://ref.ly/John27:38) · [HEB 5:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:12) · [HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14) · [JAS 2:15](https://ref.ly/Heb2:15)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle differences of meaning in the various terms listed here as meaning ‘food,’ but it is impossible to determine such distinctions in meaning from NT contexts. Perhaps τροφή and διατροφή are somewhat more generic in meaning and may suggest a greater emphasis upon nourishment (see footnote b). At the same time, βρῶσις\[c] and βρῶμα\[a] may imply solid substantive food, but it is difficult, if not impossible, to argue for such subtle connotative distinctions in meanings which are essentially generic. 2 MAT 10:10 It is possible that τροφή and διατροφή focus primarily upon the meaning of food as nourishment, and in [MAT 10:10](https://ref.ly/Matt10:10) and [1TI 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:8) it would be perfectly appropriate to use a translation meaning ‘nourishment’ rather than merely ‘food.’

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:4; Matthew 6:25; Matthew 10:10; Matthew 24:45; Luke 12:23; John 4:8; Acts 2:46; Acts 9:19; Acts 14:17; Acts 27:33; Acts 27:34; Acts 27:36; Acts 27:38; Hebrews 5:12; Hebrews 5:14; James 2:15

67\.83 · Time · Duration of Time without Reference to Points or Units of Time: Time, Spend Time, Always, Eternal, Old, Immediately, Young

## τρύβλιον (id: 005055000000000)

τρύβλιον
========

τρύβλιον (G5165)

noun, n. \| \-ου

6\.136 · Artifacts · Containers

bowl, dish a relatively deep concave dish used for holding or cooking food or liquids; usually made of clay, but also metals In the two NT occurrences ([MAT 26:23](https://ref.ly/Matt26:23); [MRK 14:20](https://ref.ly/Matt14:20)) τρύβλιον can be understood as a part of an idiom (literally ‘to dip one’s hands into the bowl with someone’) meaning ‘to share a meal with someone.’ If, however, the idiom is to be translated literally (and this is normally the case), there are certain difficulties involved, since a literal rendering of ‘to dip one’s hand into a bowl’ might mean literally putting one’s fingers or hand into a bowl rather than dipping in food which one holds in the hand. An idiomatic interpretation of ‘sharing a meal with someone’ or ‘eating together with’ may be preferable. But if one does translate the idiom somewhat literally, it is important in some languages to render this phrase as ‘to dip food into a bowl together with someone’ or ‘to jointly dip food into sauce.’

[MAT 26:23](https://ref.ly/Matt26:23) · [MRK 14:20](https://ref.ly/Matt14:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:23; Mark 14:20

## τρυγών (id: 005057000000000)

τρυγών
======

τρυγών (G5167)

noun, f. \| \-όνος

4\.44 · Animals · Birds

dove, pigeon Asiatic Rock dove: bird with a blue\-gray color with a pinkish sheen to the neck feathers and a black tip on its tail; lives in large colonies and eats mainly seeds; courts, mates, and has nests several times a year; nests on rock ledges; Columba via; used as food and for sacrifices; regarded as swift, docile, and innocent Though in English a relatively clear distinction is made between ‘doves’ (which have pointed tails) and ‘pigeons’ (which have square off tails), there seems to be no such distinction in the use of περιστερά and τρυγών in the Greek of the New Testament.  
There are, however, certain problems involved in the connotations of terms relating to pigeons or doves. According to ancient zoology, the dove was thought to have no bile, and consequently, therefore, to be a very peaceful and clean bird. It thus became a symbol of Christian virtue and of gentleness (as in [MAT 10:16](https://ref.ly/Matt10:16)). In reality, however, doves and pigeons are quite aggressive, and a group of pigeons are frequently known to peck an injured bird to death. Therefore, in some societies pigeons or doves are not regarded as gentle or peaceful, but rather as wicked and harmful. In fact, in some cultures doves are thought to be symbols of death and of evil. Under such circumstances it is important, therefore, to have some marginal note so as to indicate clearly the symbolic significance of such birds in biblical contexts.

[LUK 2:24](https://ref.ly/Mark2:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 2:24


## τρυμαλιά (id: 005058000000000)

τρυμαλιά
========

τρυμαλιά (G5168)

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς \| τρύπημα

6\.216 · Artifacts · Miscellaneous

hole a small opening1 (used in the NT only with reference to the so\-called ‘eye’ of a needle) The hole in a needle is variously referred to in different languages, for example, ‘the nostril of the needle,’ ‘the ear of the needle,’ ‘the mouth of the needle,’ and even ‘the anus of the needle.’

[MRK 10:25](https://ref.ly/Matt10:25)

1 The terms τρῆμα, τρύπημα, and τρυμαλιά actually belong theoretically to a domain of openings, holes, and apertures, but since these terms in the NT are associated so closely with a needle, it seems far more satisfactory to treat them together with ῥαφίς and βελόνη needle ([6\.215](#6.215)).

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 10:25

## τύπος (id: 005070000000000)

τύπος
=====

τύπος (G5179)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| τύπτω

8\.56 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

scar, wound a visible impression or trace made as the result of a blow or pressure1 Though both στίγμα\[a] ([8\.55](#8.55)) and τύπος\[a] may mean scars, there are significant differences in meaning. στίγμα\[a] bears the connotation of brand or mark of ownership, while τύπος\[a] indicates a wound or scar resulting from the shape and form of some object, for example, nails in the case of [JHN 20:25](https://ref.ly/Luke20:25).

6\.96 · Artifacts · Images and Idols

likeness, image (see {D:58\.35}) an object (not necessarily three\-dimensional) which has been formed to resemble a person, god, animal, etc. In certain contexts the referents of εἰκών\[a], τύπος\[b], and χάραγμα\[b] may have special religious significance in that they may refer to idols, but the focal component for the translator is that of a likeness or resemblance. In contexts such as [MAT 22:20](https://ref.ly/Matt22:20) an equivalent translation may be simply a picture, but in [ROM 1:23](https://ref.ly/Acts1:23) and [ACT 7:43](https://ref.ly/John7:43) one may use the same expression as is employed to render εἴδωλον\[a] idol ([6\.97](#6.97)).

[ACT 7:43](https://ref.ly/John7:43)

model, pattern a visual form designed to be imitated or copied

[1CO 10:6](https://ref.ly/Rom10:6) · [PHP 3:17](https://ref.ly/Eph3:17) · [1TH 1:7](https://ref.ly/Col1:7) · [2TH 3:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess3:9) · [1TI 4:12](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:12) · [TIT 2:7](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:7) · [1PE 5:3](https://ref.ly/Jas5:3)

1 Properly speaking, στίγμα\[a] ([8\.55](#8.55)) and τύπος\[a] ([8\.56](#8.56)) are not body parts, but may refer to features of the body which may result from some external force or object and could accordingly be classified in Domain 19 Physical Impact. ## τύπτω (id: 005071000000000)

τύπτω
=====

τύπτω (G5180)

verb \| ἀντίτυπος · ἐντυπόω · τυμπανίζω · τυπικῶς · τύπος · ὑποτύπωσις

19\.1 · Physical Impact · Hit, Strike

to hit, to strike, to beat to strike or hit an object, one or more times Note that the imperfect tense may be used of a repeated action, and therefore the translation ‘beat.’ ἔτυπτεν τὸ στῆθος αὐτοῦ ‘he beat his breast’ [LUK 18:13](https://ref.ly/Mark18:13). The action of ‘beating the breast’ in [LUK 18:13](https://ref.ly/Mark18:13) is symbolic in that it has the meaning of repentance and contrition. In other languages, however, the expression ‘to beat the breast’ may constitute a symbol of pride or self\-flattery. In some languages the equivalent of the biblical expression ‘to beat the breast’ is ‘to strike the head’ or ‘to grasp the abdomen.’

## τυφλός (id: 005076000000000)

τυφλός
======

τυφλός (G5185)

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| τυφλόω

24\.38 · Sensory Events and States · See

unable to see, blind pertaining to being unable to see

[MAT 9:27](https://ref.ly/Matt9:27) · [MAT 9:28](https://ref.ly/Matt9:28) · [MAT 11:5](https://ref.ly/Matt11:5) · [MAT 12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22) · [MAT 15:14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:14) · [MAT 15:14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:14) · [MAT 15:30](https://ref.ly/Matt15:30) · [MAT 15:31](https://ref.ly/Matt15:31) · [MAT 20:30](https://ref.ly/Matt20:30) · [MAT 21:14](https://ref.ly/Matt21:14) · [MRK 8:22](https://ref.ly/Matt8:22) · [MRK 8:23](https://ref.ly/Matt8:23) · [MRK 10:46](https://ref.ly/Matt10:46) · [MRK 10:49](https://ref.ly/Matt10:49) · [MRK 10:51](https://ref.ly/Matt10:51) · [LUK 4:18](https://ref.ly/Mark4:18) · [LUK 6:39](https://ref.ly/Mark6:39) · [LUK 6:39](https://ref.ly/Mark6:39) · [LUK 7:21](https://ref.ly/Mark7:21) · [LUK 7:22](https://ref.ly/Mark7:22) · [LUK 14:13](https://ref.ly/Mark14:13) · [LUK 14:21](https://ref.ly/Mark14:21) · [LUK 18:35](https://ref.ly/Mark18:35) · [JHN 5:3](https://ref.ly/Luke5:3) · [JHN 9:1](https://ref.ly/Luke9:1) · [JHN 9:2](https://ref.ly/Luke9:2) · [JHN 9:13](https://ref.ly/Luke9:13) · [JHN 9:17](https://ref.ly/Luke9:17) · [JHN 9:18](https://ref.ly/Luke9:18) · [JHN 9:19](https://ref.ly/Luke9:19) · [JHN 9:20](https://ref.ly/Luke9:20) · [JHN 9:24](https://ref.ly/Luke9:24) · [JHN 9:25](https://ref.ly/Luke9:25) · [JHN 9:32](https://ref.ly/Luke9:32) · [JHN 9:41](https://ref.ly/Luke9:41) · [JHN 10:21](https://ref.ly/Luke10:21) · [JHN 11:37](https://ref.ly/Luke11:37) · [ACT 13:11](https://ref.ly/John13:11)

32\.42 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

unable to understand, incapable of comprehending, blind (a figurative extension of meaning of τυφλός\[a] ‘unable to see, blind,’ [24\.38](#24.38)) pertaining to not being able to understand In a number of languages it is possible to preserve the figurative meaning of ‘blind’; in certain instances, however, part of the figurative meaning may be retained by translating ‘not able to see how to live’ or ‘not able to see the truth.’

[MAT 15:14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:14) · [MAT 15:14](https://ref.ly/Matt15:14) · [MAT 23:16](https://ref.ly/Matt23:16) · [MAT 23:17](https://ref.ly/Matt23:17) · [MAT 23:19](https://ref.ly/Matt23:19) · [MAT 23:24](https://ref.ly/Matt23:24) · [MAT 23:26](https://ref.ly/Matt23:26) · [JHN 9:39](https://ref.ly/Luke9:39) · [JHN 9:40](https://ref.ly/Luke9:40) · [ROM 2:19](https://ref.ly/Acts2:19) · [2PE 1:9](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:9) · [REV 3:17](https://ref.ly/Jude3:17)

## τυφλόω (id: 005077000000000)

τυφλόω
======

τυφλόω (G5186)

verb \| τυφλός

32\.43 · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

to make someone not understand, to remove someone’s understanding (a causative derivative of τυφλός\[b] unable to understand, [32\.42](#32.42)) to cause someone not to be able to understand

[2CO 4:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:4)

32\.25 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

**Collocation:** τυφλόω τοὺς ὀφθαλμούς

to cause to not understand, to make unable to comprehend (an idiom, literally: to blind the eyes) to cause someone to no longer have the capacity for understanding Though in some languages there is a close relationship between the eyes and comprehension, in many languages it is simply impossible to use the idiom ‘to blind the eyes’ in speaking of ‘causing someone not to understand.’ The problem becomes particularly difficult in speaking of ‘darkness blinding the eyes’ as in [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11). People can understand how ‘bright light would blind the eyes,’ but it would be strange indeed to think of ‘darkness’ having such an effect. In the context of [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11), the darkness is, of course, not literal darkness but a state of sinfulness. Therefore, in some languages it may be necessary to translate ‘their sinfulness has made it impossible for them to understand’ or ‘because they sin, they cannot understand.’

[JHN 12:40](https://ref.ly/Luke12:40) · [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 4:4; John 12:40; 1 John 2:11


## τυφόω (id: 005078000000000)

τυφόω

τυφόω (G5187) — τυφόομαι

verb \| τύφομαι

88\.218 · (τυφόομαι) · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Arrogance, Haughtiness, Pride

to be insanely arrogant, to be extremely proud, to be very arrogant (a figurative extension of meaning of τυφόομαι ‘to be crazy, to be demented,’ not occurring in the NT) to be so arrogant as to be practically demented

[1TI 3:6](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:6) · [1TI 6:4](https://ref.ly/2Thess6:4) · [2TI 3:4](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:4)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 3:6; 1 Timothy 6:4; 2 Timothy 3:4


## τύφω (id: 005079000000000)

τύφω
====

τύφω (G5188) — τύφομαι

verb \| τεφρόω · τυφόομαι

14\.64 · (τύφομαι) · Physical Events and States · Burning

to smolder, to flicker the process of burning slowly, with accompanying smoke and relatively little glow In [MAT 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20) the burning of the wick may be described as ‘to burn very slowly’ or ‘to burn just a little,’ but it may be more satisfactory to render τύφομαι in terms of the amount of light which is shown, for example, ‘causing just a little light’ or ‘shining only a little as it burns.’

[MAT 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:20


## τυφωνικός (id: 005080000000000)

τυφωνικός
=========

τυφωνικός (G5189)

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| Τυφῶν

14\.7 · Physical Events and States · Wind

of a violent, strong wind (derivative of τυφῶν ‘Typhon,’ the legendary father of the winds, not occurring in the NT) pertaining to a very strong wind Expressions for strong winds often differ on the basis of two important features: (1\) the strength or violence of the wind and (2\) the duration of the wind. For example, in English terms such as squall and tornado indicate violent but short periods of blowing, while hurricane or typhoon indicates a storm which takes a much longer period of time to pass. In [ACT 27:14](https://ref.ly/John27:14) the reference is obviously to the latter type of storm, called typhoon, hurricane, or monsoon, depending upon the region in which such violent and protracted storms occur.

[ACT 27:14](https://ref.ly/John27:14)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 27:14
